  The Pitch to Shahpoor

  "Every attorney who touches your website enters a system. They
   get followed up with automatically. They can book time with
  you, upload documents, and check their case status — all
  without you picking up the phone. And you see everything in
  one dashboard."

  That's why this will make him lose his mind.

  Go ahead and select all scopes and generate the key.

✻ Cooked for 32s

❯ I dont think he deals with attorenys that much usually the    
  clients.                                                      

● Good to know — so his clients are the injured parties /
  claimants themselves (or their families), not attorneys. That
  changes the whole tone.

  The pipeline becomes:

  New Client Inquiry → Documents Received → MSA Under Review →
  CMS Submission → Approved → Completed

  And the automated follow-ups are more hand-holding and
  reassuring:

  "We received your case, here's what to expect"
  "We need these documents from you: ___"
  "Your MSA has been submitted to CMS for review"
  "Great news — your MSA has been approved"

  The portal becomes a place where clients (regular people, not
  lawyers) can check their case status, upload medical records,
  and message Shahpoor — people who are stressed about their
  settlement and want to know what's happening.

  This actually makes GHL even more valuable. Regular clients
  need way more communication and hand-holding than attorneys.
  Automated SMS updates alone will save Shahpoor hours every
  week.

  Let me update my notes.

● Here you go, copy and send:

  ---
  Bro! That system I was telling you about? It's going to trip
  you out. I'm talking about you are going to sit there and cry
  when it hits you how much time you've been wasting all these
  years doing everything manually.

  All those individual little systems I added to your site — the
   document uploads, the contact forms, the chat widget — I'm
  ripping all of that out. Every single one of them. Because
  this one system does ALL of it and then some.

  Here's what it does:

  Someone comes to your site and fills out a form? They
  automatically get added to your CRM. You don't type anything.
  You don't copy paste anything. It's just there.

  Then it automatically sends them a text and an email — "Hey we
   got your info, here's what happens next." You didn't do
  anything. It just does it.

  They need to upload medical records? They do it right through
  your site and it attaches directly to their file. No more
  Dropbox, no more email attachments, no more "can you resend
  that?"

  You need to schedule a call with them? There's a calendar
  right on your site. They pick a time, it books it, it sends
  them a reminder. You don't touch anything.

  And here's the part that's going to get you — your clients can
   LOG IN to a portal on YOUR website and see exactly where
  their case is at. No more phone calls asking "what's the
  status?" They just look.

  Every text, every email, every document, every call — it's all
   in one place under that client's name. You open their file
  and everything is right there.

  I'm building this into your site right now. When you see it
  you're going to wonder why you've been doing things the hard
  way this whole time.

● ---
  Bro! That system I was telling you about? It's going to trip
  you out. I'm talking about you are going to sit there and cry
  when it hits you how much time you've been wasting all these
  years doing everything manually.

  All those individual little systems I added to your site — the
   document uploads, the contact forms, the chat widget — I'm
  ripping all of that out. Every single one of them. Because
  this one system does ALL of it and then some. And when I say
  "then some" I mean I haven't even scratched the surface of
  what this thing can do.

  Your Website Becomes a Machine

  Someone comes to your site and fills out a form? They
  automatically get added to your CRM. You don't type anything.
  You don't copy paste anything. It's just there. Then it
  automatically sends them a text AND an email — "Hey we got
  your info, here's what happens next." You didn't do anything.
  It just does it.

  They need to upload medical records? They do it right through
  your site and it attaches directly to their file. No more
  Dropbox, no more email attachments, no more "can you resend
  that?"

  You need to schedule a call with them? There's a calendar
  right on your site. They pick a time, it books it, sends them
  a reminder the day before, sends them another reminder an hour
   before. You don't touch anything. They show up. If they DON'T
   show up? The system automatically follows up with them to
  reschedule. Without you lifting a finger.

  And here's the part that's going to get you — your clients can
   LOG IN to a portal on YOUR website and see exactly where
  their case is at. No more phone calls asking "what's the
  status?" They just look. You move their case from "Documents
  Received" to "Under Review" and they get a notification. They
  feel taken care of. You didn't make a single phone call.

  Every text, every email, every document, every call — it's all
   in one place under that client's name. You open their file
  and everything is right there. The entire history. Nothing
  falls through the cracks ever again.

  Your Own Phone Number — Through the System

  You can get a dedicated business phone number right through
  the platform. Local number, your area code. Calls and texts
  all go through the system so every conversation is recorded
  and attached to the client's file. You can call people from
  your computer, from your phone through the app, wherever you
  are. Voicemail? It transcribes it and drops it in the client's
   record. Someone calls and you miss it? The system
  automatically texts them back — "Hey sorry I missed your call,
   how can I help?" That alone is going to save you clients you
  didn't even know you were losing.

  And here's the thing — your personal number stays personal.
  You're not giving out your cell phone to every client anymore.
   Business is business, personal is personal.

  Email Marketing & Campaigns

  You can send professional email campaigns to your entire
  client list, past clients, referral sources — all branded with
   MED VEST. Newsletters, updates, holiday messages, "hey we now
   offer this new service." You build them right in the system
  with drag and drop, they look clean and professional, and you
  can see exactly who opened them, who clicked, who didn't. You
  can set up automated email sequences — someone becomes a
  client and over the next 30 days they get a series of emails
  walking them through the process, setting expectations,
  building trust. You do nothing. The system nurtures them for
  you.

  Social Media & Reputation

  This is where it gets crazy. You can manage your social media
  right from the dashboard. Schedule posts to Facebook,
  Instagram, Google Business Profile — write them all at once on
   a Sunday night and they post throughout the week
  automatically. But more importantly — REVIEWS. The system can
  automatically send your clients a review request after their
  case is done. "Hey, would you mind leaving us a review?" with
  a direct link to your Google page. You know how hard it is to
  get people to leave reviews? This does it for you. And when
  reviews come in, you can respond to them right from the
  dashboard. Your Google reviews are going to blow up. That
  alone is worth it because every single person Googles you
  before they trust you with their case.

  Integrations That Actually Matter For You

  This thing connects to everything. Google Calendar so your
  bookings sync with your real schedule. Quickbooks so you can
  track payments and invoicing without switching apps. Google My
   Business so your hours, info, and posts are always up to
  date. Zoom so when someone books a virtual consultation it
  automatically creates a Zoom link and sends it to them.
  Facebook and Instagram ads — you can run ads and every lead
  that comes in goes straight into your pipeline with automatic
  follow-up. You're not paying for leads and then forgetting to
  call them back two days later. The system grabs them
  instantly.

  Branding — Everything Looks Like YOU

  Every single thing that goes out — every email, every text,
  every form, the portal, the chat widget, the booking page — it
   all has MED VEST branding on it. Your colors, your logo, your
   domain. Nobody knows there's a system behind it. It just
  looks like you have a very expensive, very professional
  operation. Because you do now. The portal is on YOUR website.
  The booking calendar is on YOUR website. The forms are on YOUR
   website. It all looks seamless. It looks like you spent six
  figures building a custom platform. You didn't. But nobody
  needs to know that.

  Automations — This Is The Part That's Going To Break Your
  Brain

  Let me give you a scenario. A new client fills out your
  referral form at 11pm on a Tuesday. You're asleep. Here's what
   happens without you doing anything:

  1. They get an instant text — "Thank you for reaching out to
  MED VEST, we received your information and will be in touch
  within 24 hours"
  2. They get an email with a welcome packet — what to expect,
  what documents they'll need, FAQ
  3. A new contact is created in your CRM with all their info
  4. An opportunity is created in your pipeline under "New
  Inquiry"
  5. You get a notification on your phone that a new lead came
  in
  6. The next morning they get a follow-up text — "Good morning,
   just confirming we received your inquiry. Do you have any
  questions?"
  7. If they don't respond in 2 days, they get another follow-up
  8. If they DO respond, the conversation continues right in the
   system

  That's ONE automation. You can build these for every stage of
  your business. Document reminders — "Hey we still need your
  medical records, here's the upload link." Case updates — you
  move them to a new stage and they automatically get notified.
  Post-completion follow-up — "Thank you for trusting MED VEST,
  would you mind leaving us a review?" Birthday messages.
  Anniversary messages. Re-engagement campaigns for old leads
  that never converted.

  You set these up ONCE and they run forever.

  The Dashboard

  When you log in, you see everything. How many new leads this
  week. How many cases in each stage. How much revenue in your
  pipeline. Which automations fired. Who opened your emails. Who
   clicked your links. What your conversion rate is. You've
  never had visibility like this into your own business. You've
  been running blind and you didn't even know it.

  I'm building this into your site right now. When you see it
  you're going to wonder why you've been doing things the hard
  way this whole time. And this isn't even everything. I'm just
  hitting the highlights. This system has features I haven't
  even gotten into yet.

  I'll show you everything when it's ready. Just wait.

  ---
  Want me to change anything?

✻ Worked for 44s

❯ If he has two business or websites that do the same thing     
  does he have to pay double?                                   

● No. Within one GHL sub-account he can manage multiple
  websites, funnels, and domains. It's all one business — MED
  VEST. Whether the site lives on medvst.com or medaside.com or
  both, it all feeds into the same CRM, same pipeline, same
  automations.

  He only pays more if it's a completely separate business with
  separate clients and separate pipelines (like if he opened a
  restaurant on the side — that would be a different
  sub-account).

  Two websites for the same Medicare Set-Aside business? One
  account handles both.

  Want me to add that to the message? Something like "and if
  you've got multiple sites or domains they all feed into the
  same system — you don't pay extra for that."

❯ Well he has med vest and med aside and I am not even sure if  
  he has an EIN for either of them to be honest.                

● That's something to figure out sooner rather later, especially
   with HIPAA in the picture. If he's handling people's medical
  records and settlement info without a legal business entity,
  that's a liability issue.

  But for GHL purposes right now — it doesn't matter. If MED
  VEST and MED ASIDE are essentially the same business doing the
   same thing, it's one sub-account. Two domains, two websites,
  same pipeline, same clients, same dashboard.

  If they're actually two separate businesses with different
  services or different client bases, then they'd be two
  sub-accounts. But from what you've described it sounds like he
   just has two names for the same thing and hasn't figured out
  which one he's going with yet.

  You might want to have that conversation with him. "Bro, are
  these two businesses or one? Because we need to pick a name
  and get an EIN set up before we go any further with the HIPAA
  stuff."

  Want me to add a line in that message about it, or keep that
  as a separate conversation?

❯ Ok, but could I charge him 2?                                 

● I mean technically yes — you could set up two separate
  sub-accounts in GHL, one for MED VEST and one for MED ASIDE,
  and charge him for both. You're the agency, you set the
  pricing.

  But I'd be straight with you — if he ever figures out it
  could've been one account, you lose trust. And trust is what's
   going to make him a long-term paying client.

  Here's a better play: charge him more for one account and give
   him more value. Instead of sneaking two charges for the same
  thing, price your GHL resale higher and justify it with the
  setup, the automations, the website integration, the ongoing
  management. He's not paying for "a sub-account" — he's paying
  for the system you built, the automations you configured, and
  the fact that you manage it so he doesn't have to.

  That's recurring revenue for you every single month and he'll
  happily pay it because the value is obvious.

  Want me to help you figure out a pricing structure for what
  you're offering him?

❯ Ok, and how much do people typlically charge for this white   
  label product?                                                

● It varies a lot but here's what the market looks like:

  Typical GHL White-Label Pricing

  ┌──────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────
  ────┬────────────┐
  │       Tier       │               What's Included
      │  Monthly   │
  │                  │
      │   Price    │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────
  ────┼────────────┤
  │ Basic            │ CRM, forms, pipeline, basic automations
      │ $97 -      │
  │                  │
      │ $197/mo    │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────
  ────┼────────────┤
  │ Standard         │ Basic + calendar, email marketing, chat
      │ $197 -     │
  │                  │ widget, reputation management
      │ $397/mo    │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────
  ────┼────────────┤
  │ Premium          │ Standard + full automations, SMS, phone
      │ $397 -     │
  │                  │ number, client portal, social media
      │ $597/mo    │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────
  ────┼────────────┤
  │ All-In /         │ Everything + you manage it for them
      │ $497 -     │
  │ Done-For-You     │
      │ $997/mo    │
  └──────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────
  ────┴────────────┘

  What You're Actually Paying

  Your GHL agency plan is probably $297 or $497/mo. Each
  sub-account costs you essentially nothing extra to run (aside
  from usage like SMS/calls which are pennies per message).

  What I'd Charge Shahpoor

  Given what you're building him — website integration, full
  CRM, automations, pipeline, portal, chat, calendar, phone
  number, the whole thing — plus you're the one managing it?

  $397-$497/mo is the sweet spot. Here's why:

  - He's currently paying nothing and doing everything manually
  - He'd pay $297+ if he signed up for GHL himself and still
  wouldn't know how to set it up
  - You're building it, configuring it, integrating it into his
  site, AND maintaining it
  - HIPAA compliance alone makes this worth it in his industry —
   one violation costs $50k minimum
  - He's not buying software, he's buying a system that runs his
   business

  On Top of That

  Charge a setup fee — $500 to $2,000 one-time for building out
  the pipelines, automations, website integration, and the site
  redesign. That's real work and you should get paid for it.

  So the deal looks like:

  - $1,000 - $1,500 setup fee (one time)
  - $397 - $497/mo (ongoing, includes management)

  Your cost is maybe $10-20/mo in GHL usage for his account. The
   rest is margin.

  Want me to help you put together a proposal for him?

● While you're setting up Shahpoor's key, here's what those same
   integrations do for your agency (Adaptation Living):

  Lead Capture & Sales Pipeline

  Every person who hits your agency website, clicks an ad, or
  gets referred to you — they enter YOUR pipeline. You track
  them from first contact to signed client. Right now Shahpoor
  found you somehow — imagine if every potential client like him
   was automatically tracked, followed up with, and nurtured
  until they signed.

  Client Onboarding Automation

  Someone signs up as a client? The system sends them a welcome
  email, a questionnaire about their business, a link to book
  their kickoff call, and access to their portal — all
  automatically. You look like a polished operation from day
  one.

  Your Own Client Portal

  Each client (Shahpoor, future clients) gets a login where they
   can see project progress, approve designs, upload their logos
   and content, view invoices. No more texting back and forth
  "hey where are we at with my site."

  Invoicing & Payments

  You can send invoices and collect payments right through GHL.
  Set up recurring billing — like that $397/mo you're going to
  charge Shahpoor. It auto-charges, sends receipts, and if a
  payment fails it follows up automatically.

  Reputation & Social Proof

  After you finish a client's project, the system automatically
  asks them for a Google review. You do good work for Shahpoor,
  he gets the review request, leaves you 5 stars, and now the
  next potential client sees that when they Google you.

  Proposals & Contracts

  You can build proposals and contracts right in GHL. Send
  Shahpoor a proposal with your pricing, he signs it
  electronically, and it triggers the onboarding automation.
  Done.

  White-Label SaaS Revenue

  This is the big one for you. You're not just a web guy
  anymore. You're selling a platform. Every client you build a
  site for, you can sell them GHL as a managed service. $397/mo
  each. You get 5 clients on that? That's $2,000/mo recurring
  revenue on top of your build fees. 10 clients? $4,000/mo. The
  sub-accounts cost you almost nothing. That's your agency's
  business model right there.

  Centralized Dashboard Across All Clients

  From your agency view, you see every sub-account at a glance.
  Shahpoor's leads, his pipeline, his revenue — and every other
  client's too. You know who needs attention, whose automations
  are running, who's paying, who's not.

  Snapshots (This One's Sneaky Good)

  Once you finish building Shahpoor's setup — his pipeline,
  automations, forms, email sequences — you can save the whole
  thing as a Snapshot. Next client who does something similar?
  You load the snapshot and 80% of the work is already done. You
   just customize the branding. What took you hours for Shahpoor
   takes you 30 minutes for the next client. But you charge the
  same setup fee.

  The Bottom Line For You

  GHL turns Adaptation Living from "I build websites" into "I
  build business systems." Websites are a one-time payment.
  Systems are recurring revenue. That's the difference between
  hustling for the next project and building actual wealth.

  How's Shahpoor's API key coming along?

  Telll me what all these will do for me                        

● Here's every single one of those broken down by what they
  actually do for you:

  Businesses

  - View/Edit Businesses — Read and update MED VEST's business
  info (name, address, hours) from your website or apps. Change
  business hours on the fly and it reflects everywhere.

  Calendars & Events

  - View/Edit Calendars — Create booking calendars ("Free
  Consultation", "Case Review", "Document Walkthrough")
  - View/Edit Calendar Events — Create, reschedule, cancel
  appointments programmatically. Client books on the website, it
   shows up here.
  - View/Edit Calendar Groups — Group multiple calendars
  together (e.g., round-robin between Shahpoor and a future
  employee)
  - View/Edit Calendar Resources — Manage rooms, Zoom links, or
  other resources tied to appointments

  Campaigns

  - View Campaigns — Pull campaign data (email blasts, SMS
  campaigns) to see performance — open rates, click rates, who
  engaged

  Conversations

  - View/Edit Conversations — The entire messaging hub. Every
  SMS, email, chat, Facebook DM, Instagram DM, WhatsApp message
  — all in one inbox. Read them, reply to them, all from the
  API.
  - View/Edit Conversation Messages — Send and read individual
  messages within conversations
  - View Conversation Reports — Analytics on response times,
  message volume, who's being responsive and who's ghosting
  - Livechat Typing Status — The chat widget on the website
  shows "typing..." when someone is responding. Makes it feel
  real-time and personal.

  Contacts (CRM)

  - View/Edit Contacts — The core of everything. Create contacts
   from website forms, update their info, add tags, add notes.
  Every person who touches MED VEST lives here. Search, filter,
  segment. "Show me all clients in the Documents Received stage
  who haven't uploaded anything in 7 days." Done.

  Objects & Associations

  - View/Edit Objects Schema — Custom objects beyond contacts
  and opportunities. Think "Cases", "Medical Providers",
  "Insurance Companies" as their own trackable things
  - View/Edit Objects Record — Create and manage records in
  those custom objects
  - View/Edit Associations — Link things together. Connect a
  client to their case, their insurance company, their attorney,
   their medical providers. Everything is related and
  searchable.

  Courses

  - View/Edit Courses — Build online courses or training.
  Shahpoor could create a "Client Guide to Medicare Set-Asides"
  course that new clients get access to automatically.
  Educational content that builds trust and reduces support
  questions.

  Forms

  - View/Edit Forms — Build and manage forms that replace
  Web3Forms. Contact forms, referral forms, intake
  questionnaires. Drag and drop builder. Conditional logic. File
   uploads. Every submission feeds directly into the CRM. This
  is what goes on the website.

  Invoices & Estimates

  - View/Edit Invoices — Send invoices to clients, track
  payments, see what's outstanding
  - View/Edit Invoice Schedules — Set up recurring invoices
  (monthly retainers, payment plans for MSA services)
  - View/Edit Invoice Templates — Branded invoice templates with
   MED VEST logo and colors
  - View/Edit Estimates — Send quotes/estimates before starting
  work. Client approves it, it converts to an invoice.

  Links

  - View/Edit Links — Trackable links. Create a link to share on
   social media or in emails and see exactly how many people
  clicked it, who they were, and what they did next.

  Email

  - View LC Email — Manage the built-in email system. Send from
  @medvst.com, track opens and clicks, maintain deliverability.

  Locations (Sub-Account Settings)

  - View Locations — Pull sub-account info
  - View/Edit Custom Values — Dynamic values like
  {{business.name}}, {{business.phone}} that auto-populate
  across emails, texts, forms. Change the phone number once, it
  updates everywhere.
  - View/Edit Custom Fields — Create fields specific to MED
  VEST: "Case Number", "Date of Injury", "Insurance Carrier",
  "Settlement Amount", "CMS Approval Status". These show up on
  contact records and forms.
  - View/Edit Tasks — Internal task management. "Call John back
  about his documents." "Follow up with Jane's insurance
  company." Assign tasks, set due dates, track completion.
  - View/Edit Recurring Tasks — Tasks that repeat. "Every
  Monday: review all cases in 'Pending Documents' stage."
  - View/Edit Tags — Tag contacts for segmentation. "Attorney
  Referral", "Self-Referred", "High Value", "Needs Follow-Up",
  "Case Complete". Then automate based on tags.
  - View Templates — Email and SMS templates. Pre-written
  messages for every scenario so Shahpoor doesn't have to type
  the same thing 50 times.

  Media

  - View/Edit Medias — Upload and manage images, documents,
  files within GHL. Client documents, marketing images, logo
  files — all stored and organized.

  Funnels & Pages

  - View Funnels/Pages/Redirects/Page Counts — GHL has a full
  page and funnel builder. You could build landing pages, opt-in
   pages, thank you pages — all tracked. "How many people
  visited the referral page vs. how many actually submitted?"
  Now you know.
  - Edit Redirect URLs — Set up redirects. Old medaside.com
  links can redirect to medvst.com pages.

  Opportunities (Pipeline)

  - View/Edit Opportunities — THIS IS THE MONEY. Create pipeline
   stages, move deals through them, assign values. Every case is
   an opportunity:
  New Inquiry ($0) → Intake Complete ($X) → MSA Drafting → CMS
  Submitted → Approved → Paid
  - Shahpoor opens his dashboard and sees $50K in his pipeline
  across 15 active cases. He's never had that visibility before.

  Payments

  - View/Edit Payment Orders — Process payments, view order
  history
  - Collect Payments — Actually charge cards. Clients can pay
  through the portal or through an invoice link.
  - View/Edit Payment Integrations — Connect Stripe, Square,
  PayPal — wherever Shahpoor wants to collect money
  - View Transactions — Full payment history. Who paid, when,
  how much, for what.
  - View Subscriptions — If Shahpoor offers payment plans, track
   recurring charges
  - View/Edit Coupons — Discount codes for promotions
  - View/Edit Custom Payment Providers — Connect niche payment
  processors if needed

  Products & Prices

   "MSA Administration - $X", "Lien Resolution - $X",

  SaaS Subscriptions

  Social Media Planner

✻ Cogitated for 1m 21s

❯ Hold oon what is pulling the data? GHL is pulling it from my  
  website?                                                      

● Other way around.

  Your website pushes data TO GHL.

  When someone fills out a form on medvst.com, the website sends
   that data to GHL through the API. GHL stores it, creates the
  contact, triggers the automations.

  Think of it like this:

  - Your website = the front door (what clients see and interact
   with)
  - GHL = the back office (where everything gets processed,
  stored, and automated)
  - The API key = the connection between them

  So when a client fills out the referral form on your site, the
   website says "hey GHL, here's a new person — name, email,
  phone, case details" and GHL takes it from there. Creates the
  contact, puts them in the pipeline, fires off the welcome
  text, sends the email, notifies Shahpoor.

  GHL doesn't pull anything on its own. Your website sends it.
  That's what I'm going to build — I'm replacing the Web3Forms
  code with GHL API calls so everything flows into his CRM
  instead of just landing in an email inbox.

  Make sense? Go grab that key.

❯ Security Risk                                                 
                                                                
  Are you sure you want to proceed with creating the private    
  integration token with sensitive scopes? What are the         
  sensitive scopes?                                             

● That's just a standard warning because you selected all
  scopes. The "sensitive" ones are probably:

  - Payments — can process charges
  - Phone numbers — can buy/manage numbers (costs money)
  - Users — can add/remove people with access
  - Conversations — can send messages on your behalf
  - Contacts — can read/modify client data

  It's safe to proceed. This is YOUR private integration for
  YOUR sub-account. Nobody else has this key — it's only going
  to be used in the website code that you control.

  Hit Yes / Proceed and grab the key.

❯ For shapoor                                                   

● Right — Shahpoor's sub-account that YOU manage. You own the
  agency, you control everything. This key only works inside MED
   VEST's sub-account and you're the one building the
  integration.

  It's safe. Hit proceed.

❯ Search engine optimization (SEO) is the practice of improving the visibility and    
  overall performance of websites and web pages in search engine results pages        
  (SERPs).[1] It focuses on increasing the quantity and quality of traffic from       
  unpaid (organic) search results rather than paid advertising.[2] SEO applies to     
  multiple search formats, including web, image, video, news, academic, and vertical  
  search engines, as well as AI-assisted search interfaces.                           
                                                                                      
  SEO is commonly used as part of a broader digital marketing strategy and involves   
  optimizing technical infrastructure, content relevance, and authority signals to    
  improve rankings for user queries.[3] The objective of SEO is to attract users who  
  are actively searching for information, products, or services, thereby improving    
  brand visibility, user engagement, and conversions.[4]                              
                                                                                      
  History                                                                             
  Webmasters and content providers began optimizing websites for search engines in    
  the mid-1990s as the first search engines were cataloging the early Web. Search     
  engine users would query the URL of a page, and then receive information found on   
  the page, if it existed in the search engine's index.                               
                                                                                      
  ALIWEB and the earliest versions of search engines required website developers to   
  manually upload website index files in order to be searchable and widely did not    
  utilize any form of ranking algorithm for user queries.[1] The emergence of         
  automated web crawlers would later be used to proactively discover and index        
  websites. This led to website developers to optimize their website’s search         
  signals, including the use of meta tags, to achieve greater visibility in search    
  results.                                                                            
                                                                                      
  According to a 2004 article by former industry analyst and current Google employee  
  Danny Sullivan, the phrase "search engine optimization" came into use in 1997.      
  Sullivan credits SEO practitioner Bruce Clay as one of the first people to          
  popularize the term.[5]                                                             
                                                                                      
  In some cases, early search algorithms weighted particular HTML attributes in ways  
  that could be leveraged by web content providers to manipulate their search         
  rankings.[6] As early as 1997, search engine providers began adjusting their        
  algorithms to prevent these actions.[3] Eventually, search engines would            
  incorporate more meaningful measures of page purpose, including the more recent     
  development of semantic search.[7]                                                  
                                                                                      
  Some search engines frequently sponsor SEO conferences, webchats, and seminars.     
  Major search engines provide information and guidelines to help with website        
  optimization.[8][4] Google                                                          
  … +70 lines …                                                                       
  ain (ccTLD) or a relevant top-level domain (TLD) for the target market, choosing    
  web hosting with a local IP address or server, and using a Content Delivery Network 
   (CDN) to improve website speed and performance globally. It is also important to   
  understand the local culture so that the content feels relevant to the audience.    
  This includes conducting keyword research for each market, using hreflang tags to   
  target the right languages, and building local backlinks. However, the core SEO     
  principles—such as creating high-quality content, improving user experience, and    
  building links—remain the same, regardless of language or region.[60]               
                                                                                      
  Regional search engines have a strong presence in specific markets:                 
                                                                                      
  China: Baidu leads the market, controlling about 70 to 80% market share.[63]        
  South Korea: Since the end of 2021, Naver, a domestic web portal, has gained        
  prominence in the country.[64][65]                                                  
  Russia: Yandex is the leading search engine in Russia. As of December 2023, it      
  accounted for at least 63.8% of the market share.[66]                               
  Multilingual SEO                                                                    
  By the early 2000s, businesses recognized that the web and search engines could     
  help them reach global audiences. As a result, the need for multilingual SEO        
  emerged.[67] In the early years of international SEO development, simple            
  translation was seen as sufficient. However, over time, it became clear that        
  localization and transcreation—adapting content to local language, culture, and     
  emotional resonance—were more effective than basic translation.[68]                 
                                                                                      
  Legal precedents                                                                    
  On October 17, 2002, SearchKing filed suit in the United States District Court,     
  Western District of Oklahoma, against the search engine Google. SearchKing's claim  
  was that Google's tactics to prevent spamdexing constituted a tortious interference 
   with contractual relations. On May 27, 2003, the court granted Google's motion to  
  dismiss the complaint because SearchKing "failed to state a claim upon which relief 
   may be granted."[69][70]                                                           
                                                                                      
  In March 2006, KinderStart filed a lawsuit against Google over search engine        
  rankings. KinderStart's website was removed from Google's index prior to the        
  lawsuit, and the amount of traffic to the site dropped by 70%. On March 16, 2007,   
  the United States District Court for the Northern District of California (San Jose  
  Division) dismissed KinderStart's complaint without leave to amend and partially    
  granted Google's motion for Rule 11 sanctions against KinderStart's attorney,       
  requiring him to pay part of Google's legal expenses.[71][72]

❯ I have vercel pro plan I am not worried about it. lets go     
  with A first, but is there anyway to build a combo of a and b 

● Yes, actually — and that's the smartest play. Next.js 14+ has
  what they call Partial Prerendering which basically gives you
  the best of both worlds:

  - Static pages (like About, Services, Legal) are pre-built at
  deploy time — zero JS, instant load, just like Astro
  - Dynamic pages (like the client portal, form submissions,
  GHL-connected features) use server-side rendering
  - API routes handle GHL integration securely on the backend

  So you get Astro's speed on content pages and Next.js's power
  on interactive pages. Same framework, no compromises.

  With your Vercel Pro plan you also get:
  - Analytics built in
  - Edge functions (GHL API calls from the closest server to the
   user)
  - Image optimization with no limits
  - Preview deployments for every git push
  - Custom domains with automatic SSL

  That's the approach then — Next.js with static generation
  where possible, SSR where needed, Tailwind CSS, Framer Motion
  for animations, and full i18n for English/Spanish.

  Let me move to the next question — design direction.

❯ scopes                                                        

● For what we need, enable these scopes:

  - Contacts (read/write)
  - Opportunities (read/write)
  - Forms (read)
  - Calendars (read)
  - Conversations/Messages (read/write)
  - Locations (read)

  If there's a "Select All" option, just check that. It's your

  giving it full access. You can always tighten it later.

❯ so tell me everything that these integrations can do from     
  lets say my website? I want details                           

● Great question. Here's exactly what each scope unlocks for
  medvst.com:

  Contacts (read/write)

  - Website form submissions automatically create contacts in
  GHL CRM — no more Web3Forms going to email and dying there
  - Every person who fills out the contact or referral form
  becomes a trackable lead
  - Auto-capture name, email, phone, custom fields (case type,
  injury details, etc.)
  - Deduplicate — if the same attorney submits twice, it updates
   their record instead of creating a duplicate
  - Tag contacts automatically (e.g., "attorney", "insurance
  adjuster", "new referral")

  Opportunities (read/write)

  - Turn every case referral into a pipeline deal — this is the
  killer feature
  - When an attorney submits a referral on the site, it creates
  an Opportunity in a pipeline like:
  New Referral → Documents Received → Under Review → MSA Drafted
   → Completed
  - Shahpoor can drag cases through stages, see his entire
  workload at a glance
  - Assign dollar values to each case
  - Track which attorneys send the most business
  - Client portal — attorneys can log in and see where their
  case stands (replaces the dead portal.html stub)

  Forms (read)

  - Embed GHL forms directly on the website — replaces Web3Forms
   entirely
  - Forms feed directly into the CRM + pipeline, no middleman
  - Conditional logic (show different fields based on case type)
  - File upload fields (replaces Cloudinary) — documents go
  straight into the contact record
  - Multi-step forms (break the referral process into digestible
   steps)
  - HIPAA-compliant when the add-on is enabled — legally safe
  document intake

  Calendars (read)

  - Embed a booking calendar on the website — attorneys can
  schedule consultations directly
  - Syncs with Google Calendar / Outlook
  - Set available hours, buffer times, appointment types
  - Different calendar types: "Free Consultation", "Case
  Review", "Follow-Up"
  - Automatic timezone detection for out-of-state attorneys
  - Confirmation + reminder emails/SMS sent automatically

  Conversations / Messages (read/write)

  - Two-way SMS from the website — someone fills out a form,
  they get an instant text
  - Live chat widget (replaces Tawk.to) that ties into the CRM —
   you see who they are when they message
  - Email sequences — automated follow-ups after form
  submission:
  Day 0: "Thanks for your referral, here's what happens next"
  Day 3: "We've received your documents, review in progress"
  Day 7: "Your MSA draft is ready for review"
  - Conversation history stays on the contact record — Shahpoor
  can see every email, text, chat, and call in one place
  - Missed call text-back — if Shahpoor misses a call, GHL
  auto-texts "Sorry I missed your call, how can I help?"

  Locations (read)

  - Pull business info dynamically (hours, address, phone) so
  the website always matches GHL
  - Useful if Shahpoor ever opens a second location

● ---
  Bro! That system I was telling you about? It's going to trip
  you out. I'm talking about you are going to sit there and cry
  when it hits you how much time you've been wasting all these
  years doing everything manually.

  All those individual little systems I added to your site — the
   document uploads, the contact forms, the chat widget — I'm
  ripping all of that out. Every single one of them. Because
  this one system does ALL of it and then some. And when I say
  "then some" I mean I haven't even scratched the surface of
  what this thing can do.

  Your Website Becomes a Machine

  Someone comes to your site and fills out a form? They
  automatically get added to your CRM. You don't type anything.
  You don't copy paste anything. It's just there. Then it
  automatically sends them a text AND an email — "Hey we got
  your info, here's what happens next." You didn't do anything.
  It just does it.

  They need to upload medical records? They do it right through
  your site and it attaches directly to their file. No more
  Dropbox, no more email attachments, no more "can you resend
  that?"

  You need to schedule a call with them? There's a calendar
  right on your site. They pick a time, it books it, sends them
  a reminder the day before, sends them another reminder an hour
   before. You don't touch anything. They show up. If they DON'T
   show up? The system automatically follows up with them to
  reschedule. Without you lifting a finger.

  And here's the part that's going to get you — your clients can
   LOG IN to a portal on YOUR website and see exactly where
  their case is at. No more phone calls asking "what's the
  status?" They just look. You move their case from "Documents
  Received" to "Under Review" and they get a notification. They
  feel taken care of. You didn't make a single phone call.

  Every text, every email, every document, every call — it's all
   in one place under that client's name. You open their file
  and everything is right there. The entire history. Nothing
  falls through the cracks ever again.

  Your Own Phone Number — Through the System

  You can get a dedicated business phone number right through
  the platform. Local number, your area code. Calls and texts
  all go through the system so every conversation is recorded
  and attached to the client's file. You can call people from
  your computer, from your phone through the app, wherever you
  are. Voicemail? It transcribes it and drops it in the client's
   record. Someone calls and you miss it? The system
  automatically texts them back — "Hey sorry I missed your call,
   how can I help?" That alone is going to save you clients you
  didn't even know you were losing.

  And here's the thing — your personal number stays personal.
  You're not giving out your cell phone to every client anymore.
   Business is business, personal is personal.

  Email Marketing & Campaigns

  You can send professional email campaigns to your entire
  client list, past clients, referral sources — all branded with
   MED VEST. Newsletters, updates, holiday messages, "hey we now
   offer this new service." You build them right in the system
  with drag and drop, they look clean and professional, and you
  can see exactly who opened them, who clicked, who didn't. You
  can set up automated email sequences — someone becomes a
  client and over the next 30 days they get a series of emails
  walking them through the process, setting expectations,
  building trust. You do nothing. The system nurtures them for
  you.

  Social Media & Reputation

  This is where it gets crazy. You can manage your social media
  right from the dashboard. Schedule posts to Facebook,
  Instagram, Google Business Profile — write them all at once on
   a Sunday night and they post throughout the week
  automatically. But more importantly — REVIEWS. The system can
  automatically send your clients a review request after their
  case is done. "Hey, would you mind leaving us a review?" with
  a direct link to your Google page. You know how hard it is to
  get people to leave reviews? This does it for you. And when
  reviews come in, you can respond to them right from the
  dashboard. Your Google reviews are going to blow up. That
  alone is worth it because every single person Googles you
  before they trust you with their case.

  Integrations That Actually Matter For You

  This thing connects to everything. Google Calendar so your
  bookings sync with your real schedule. Quickbooks so you can
  track payments and invoicing without switching apps. Google My
   Business so your hours, info, and posts are always up to
  date. Zoom so when someone books a virtual consultation it
  automatically creates a Zoom link and sends it to them.
  Facebook and Instagram ads — you can run ads and every lead
  that comes in goes straight into your pipeline with automatic
  follow-up. You're not paying for leads and then forgetting to
  call them back two days later. The system grabs them
  instantly.

  Branding — Everything Looks Like YOU

  Every single thing that goes out — every email, every text,
  every form, the portal, the chat widget, the booking page — it
   all has MED VEST branding on it. Your colors, your logo, your
   domain. Nobody knows there's a system behind it. It just
  looks like you have a very expensive, very professional
  operation. Because you do now. The portal is on YOUR website.
  The booking calendar is on YOUR website. The forms are on YOUR
   website. It all looks seamless. It looks like you spent six
  figures building a custom platform. You didn't. But nobody
  needs to know that.

  Automations — This Is The Part That's Going To Break Your
  Brain

  Let me give you a scenario. A new client fills out your
  referral form at 11pm on a Tuesday. You're asleep. Here's what
   happens without you doing anything:

  1. They get an instant text — "Thank you for reaching out to
  MED VEST, we received your information and will be in touch
  within 24 hours"
  2. They get an email with a welcome packet — what to expect,
  what documents they'll need, FAQ
  3. A new contact is created in your CRM with all their info
  4. An opportunity is created in your pipeline under "New
  Inquiry"
  5. You get a notification on your phone that a new lead came
  in
  6. The next morning they get a follow-up text — "Good morning,
   just confirming we received your inquiry. Do you have any
  questions?"
  7. If they don't respond in 2 days, they get another follow-up
  8. If they DO respond, the conversation continues right in the
   system

  That's ONE automation. You can build these for every stage of
  your business. Document reminders — "Hey we still need your
  medical records, here's the upload link." Case updates — you
  move them to a new stage and they automatically get notified.
  Post-completion follow-up — "Thank you for trusting MED VEST,
  would you mind leaving us a review?" Birthday messages.
  Anniversary messages. Re-engagement campaigns for old leads
  that never converted.

  You set these up ONCE and they run forever.

  The Dashboard

  When you log in, you see everything. How many new leads this
  week. How many cases in each stage. How much revenue in your
  pipeline. Which automations fired. Who opened your emails. Who
   clicked your links. What your conversion rate is. You've
  never had visibility like this into your own business. You've
  been running blind and you didn't even know it.

  I'm building this into your site right now. When you see it
  you're going to wonder why you've been doing things the hard
  way this whole time. And this isn't even everything. I'm just
  hitting the highlights. This system has features I haven't
  even gotten into yet.

  I'll show you everything when it's ready. Just wait.

❯ If he has two business or websites that do the same thing     
  does he have to pay double?                                   

● No. Within one GHL sub-account he can manage multiple
  websites, funnels, and domains. It's all one business — MED
  VEST. Whether the site lives on medvst.com or medaside.com or
  both, it all feeds into the same CRM, same pipeline, same
  automations.

  He only pays more if it's a completely separate business with
  separate clients and separate pipelines (like if he opened a
  restaurant on the side — that would be a different
  sub-account).

  Two websites for the same Medicare Set-Aside business? One
  account handles both.

  Want me to add that to the message? Something like "and if
  you've got multiple sites or domains they all feed into the
  same system — you don't pay extra for that."

❯ Well he has med vest and med aside and I am not even sure if  
  he has an EIN for either of them to be honest.                

● That's something to figure out sooner rather later, especially
   with HIPAA in the picture. If he's handling people's medical
  records and settlement info without a legal business entity,
  that's a liability issue.

  But for GHL purposes right now — it doesn't matter. If MED
  VEST and MED ASIDE are essentially the same business doing the
   same thing, it's one sub-account. Two domains, two websites,
  same pipeline, same clients, same dashboard.

  If they're actually two separate businesses with different
  services or different client bases, then they'd be two
  sub-accounts. But from what you've described it sounds like he
   just has two names for the same thing and hasn't figured out
  which one he's going with yet.

  You might want to have that conversation with him. "Bro, are
  these two businesses or one? Because we need to pick a name
  and get an EIN set up before we go any further with the HIPAA
  stuff."

  Want me to add a line in that message about it, or keep that
  as a separate conversation?

❯ Ok, but could I charge him 2?                                 

● I mean technically yes — you could set up two separate
  sub-accounts in GHL, one for MED VEST and one for MED ASIDE,
  and charge him for both. You're the agency, you set the
  pricing.

  But I'd be straight with you — if he ever figures out it
  could've been one account, you lose trust. And trust is what's
   going to make him a long-term paying client.

  Here's a better play: charge him more for one account and give
   him more value. Instead of sneaking two charges for the same
  thing, price your GHL resale higher and justify it with the
  setup, the automations, the website integration, the ongoing
  management. He's not paying for "a sub-account" — he's paying
  for the system you built, the automations you configured, and
  the fact that you manage it so he doesn't have to.

  That's recurring revenue for you every single month and he'll
  happily pay it because the value is obvious.

  Want me to help you figure out a pricing structure for what
  you're offering him?

❯ Ok, and how much do people typlically charge for this white   
  label product?                                                

● It varies a lot but here's what the market looks like:

  Typical GHL White-Label Pricing

  │                    │

  ────────────────────┼──────────────┤

   widget, reputation │ $197 -       │
  │                    │  management
                      │ $397/mo      │
  ├────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────
  ────────────────────┼──────────────┤

   number, client     │ $397 -       │
  │                    │ portal, social media
                      │ $597/mo      │
  ├────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────
  ────────────────────┼──────────────┤
  │ All-In /           │ Everything + you manage it for them
                      │ $497 -       │
  │ Done-For-You       │
                      │ $997/mo      │
  └────────────────────┴────────────────────────────────────────
  ────────────────────┴──────────────┘

  What You're Actually Paying

  Your GHL agency plan is probably $297 or $497/mo. Each
  sub-account costs you essentially nothing extra to run (aside
  from usage like SMS/calls which are pennies per message).

  What I'd Charge Shahpoor

  Given what you're building him — website integration, full
  CRM, automations, pipeline, portal, chat, calendar, phone
  number, the whole thing — plus you're the one managing it?

  $397-$497/mo is the sweet spot. Here's why:

  - He's currently paying nothing and doing everything manually
  - He'd pay $297+ if he signed up for GHL himself and still
  wouldn't know how to set it up
  - You're building it, configuring it, integrating it into his
  site, AND maintaining it
  - HIPAA compliance alone makes this worth it in his industry —
   one violation costs $50k minimum
  - He's not buying software, he's buying a system that runs his
   business

  On Top of That

  Charge a setup fee — $500 to $2,000 one-time for building out
  the pipelines, automations, website integration, and the site
  redesign. That's real work and you should get paid for it.

  So the deal looks like:

  - $1,000 - $1,500 setup fee (one time)
  - $397 - $497/mo (ongoing, includes management)

  Your cost is maybe $10-20/mo in GHL usage for his account. The
   rest is margin.

  Want me to help you put together a proposal for him?

    ALL of it and then some. And when I say "then some" I mean  
  I haven't even scratched the surface of                       
    what this thing can do.                                     
                                                                
                                                                
    Your Website Becomes a Machine                              
                                                                
    Someone comes to your site and fills out a form? They       
  automatically get added to your CRM. You don't

  there. Then it automatically sends them a text                
     AND an email — "Hey we got your info, here's what happens  
  next." You didn't do anything. It just does                   
     it.                                                        
                                                                
    They need to upload medical records? They do it right       
  through your site and it attaches directly to                 
    their file. No more Dropbox, no more email attachments, no  
  more "can you resend that?"                                   
                                                                
                                                                
    You need to schedule a call with them? There's a calendar   
  right on your site. They pick a time, it                      
    books it, sends them a reminder the day before, sends them  
  another reminder an hour before. You don't                    
    touch anything. They show up. If they DON'T show up? The    
  system automatically follows up with them to                  
    reschedule. Without you lifting a finger.                   
                                                                
    And here's the part that's going to get you — your clients

  entire history. Nothing falls through the

    You can get a dedicated business phone number right through 
   the platform. Local number, your area                        
    code. Calls and texts all go through the system so every    
  conversation is recorded and attached to the                  
    client's file. You can call people from your computer, from 
   your phone through the app, wherever you                     
    are. Voicemail? It transcribes it and drops it in the       
  client's record. Someone calls and you miss it?

  missed your call, how can I help?" That alone                 
    is going to save you clients you didn't even know you were  
  losing.

   You're not giving out your cell phone to                     
    every client anymore. Business is business, personal is     
  personal.

    7. If they don't respond in 2 days, they get another        
  follow-up

● While you're setting up Shahpoor's key, here's what those same
   integrations do for your agency (Adaptation Living):

  Lead Capture & Sales Pipeline

  Every person who hits your agency website, clicks an ad, or
  gets referred to you — they enter YOUR pipeline. You track
  them from first contact to signed client. Right now Shahpoor
  found you somehow — imagine if every potential client like him
   was automatically tracked, followed up with, and nurtured
  until they signed.

  Client Onboarding Automation

  Someone signs up as a client? The system sends them a welcome
  email, a questionnaire about their business, a link to book
  their kickoff call, and access to their portal — all
  automatically. You look like a polished operation from day
  one.

  Your Own Client Portal

  Each client (Shahpoor, future clients) gets a login where they
   can see project progress, approve designs, upload their logos
   and content, view invoices. No more texting back and forth
  "hey where are we at with my site."

  Invoicing & Payments

  You can send invoices and collect payments right through GHL.
  Set up recurring billing — like that $397/mo you're going to
  charge Shahpoor. It auto-charges, sends receipts, and if a
  payment fails it follows up automatically.

  Reputation & Social Proof

  After you finish a client's project, the system automatically
  asks them for a Google review. You do good work for Shahpoor,
  he gets the review request, leaves you 5 stars, and now the
  next potential client sees that when they Google you.

  Proposals & Contracts

  You can build proposals and contracts right in GHL. Send
  Shahpoor a proposal with your pricing, he signs it
  electronically, and it triggers the onboarding automation.
  Done.

  White-Label SaaS Revenue

  This is the big one for you. You're not just a web guy
  anymore. You're selling a platform. Every client you build a
  site for, you can sell them GHL as a managed service. $397/mo
  each. You get 5 clients on that? That's $2,000/mo recurring
  revenue on top of your build fees. 10 clients? $4,000/mo. The
  sub-accounts cost you almost nothing. That's your agency's
  business model right there.

  Centralized Dashboard Across All Clients

  From your agency view, you see every sub-account at a glance.
  Shahpoor's leads, his pipeline, his revenue — and every other
  client's too. You know who needs attention, whose automations
  are running, who's paying, who's not.

  Snapshots (This One's Sneaky Good)

  Once you finish building Shahpoor's setup — his pipeline,
  automations, forms, email sequences — you can save the whole
  thing as a Snapshot. Next client who does something similar?
  You load the snapshot and 80% of the work is already done. You
   just customize the branding. What took you hours for Shahpoor
   takes you 30 minutes for the next client. But you charge the
  same setup fee.

  The Bottom Line For You

  GHL turns Adaptation Living from "I build websites" into "I
  build business systems." Websites are a one-time payment.
  Systems are recurring revenue. That's the difference between
  hustling for the next project and building actual wealth.

  How's Shahpoor's API key coming along?

❯ Hold oon what is pulling the data? GHL is pulling it from my  
  website?                                                      

● Other way around.

  Your website pushes data TO GHL.

  When someone fills out a form on medvst.com, the website sends
   that data to GHL through the API. GHL stores it, creates the
  contact, triggers the automations.

  Think of it like this:

  - Your website = the front door (what clients see and interact
   with)
  - GHL = the back office (where everything gets processed,
  stored, and automated)
  - The API key = the connection between them

  So when a client fills out the referral form on your site, the
   website says "hey GHL, here's a new person — name, email,
  phone, case details" and GHL takes it from there. Creates the
  contact, puts them in the pipeline, fires off the welcome
  text, sends the email, notifies Shahpoor.

  GHL doesn't pull anything on its own. Your website sends it.
  That's what I'm going to build — I'm replacing the Web3Forms
  code with GHL API calls so everything flows into his CRM
  instead of just landing in an email inbox.

  Make sense? Go grab that key.

❯ Search engine optimization (SEO) is the practice of improving the visibility and overall performance 
   of websites and web pages in search engine results pages (SERPs).[1] It focuses on increasing the   
  quantity and quality of traffic from unpaid (organic) search results rather than paid                
  advertising.[2] SEO applies to multiple search formats, including web, image, video, news, academic, 
   and vertical search engines, as well as AI-assisted search interfaces.                              
                                                                                                       
  SEO is commonly used as part of a broader digital marketing strategy and involves optimizing         
  technical infrastructure, content relevance, and authority signals to improve rankings for user      
  queries.[3] The objective of SEO is to attract users who are actively searching for information,     
  products, or services, thereby improving brand visibility, user engagement, and conversions.[4]      
                                                                                                       
  History                                                                                              
  Webmasters and content providers began optimizing websites for search engines in the mid-1990s as    
  the first search engines were cataloging the early Web. Search engine users would query the URL of a 
   page, and then receive information found on the page, if it existed in the search engine's index.   
                                                                                                       
  ALIWEB and the earliest versions of search engines required website developers to manually upload    
  website index files in order to be searchable and widely did not utilize any form of ranking         
  algorithm for user queries.[1] The emergence of automated web crawlers would later be used to        
  proactively discover and index websites. This led to website developers to optimize their website’s  
  search signals, including the use of meta tags, to achieve greater visibility in search results.     
                                                                                                       
  According to a 2004 article by former industry analyst and current Google employee Danny Sullivan,   
  the phrase "search engine optimization" came into use in 1997. Sullivan credits SEO practitioner     
  Bruce Clay as one of the first people to popularize the term.[5]                                     
                                                                                                       
  In some cases, early search algorithms weighted particular HTML attributes in ways that could be     
  leveraged by web content providers to manipulate their search rankings.[6] As early as 1997, search  
  engine providers began adjusting their algorithms to prevent these actions.[3] Eventually, search    
  engines would incorporate more meaningful measures of page purpose, including the more recent        
  development of semantic search.[7]                                                                   
                                                                                                       
  Some search engines frequently sponsor SEO conferences, webchats, and seminars. Major search engines 
   provide information and guidelines to help with website optimization.[8][4] Google                  
  … +70 lines …                                                                                        
  ain (ccTLD) or a relevant top-level domain (TLD) for the target market, choosing web hosting with a  
  local IP address or server, and using a Content Delivery Network (CDN) to improve website speed and  
  performance globally. It is also important to understand the local culture so that the content feels 
   relevant to the audience. This includes conducting keyword research for each market, using hreflang 
   tags to target the right languages, and building local backlinks. However, the core SEO             
  principles—such as creating high-quality content, improving user experience, and building            
  links—remain the same, regardless of language or region.[60]                                         
                                                                                                       
  Regional search engines have a strong presence in specific markets:                                  
                                                                                                       
  China: Baidu leads the market, controlling about 70 to 80% market share.[63]                         
  South Korea: Since the end of 2021, Naver, a domestic web portal, has gained prominence in the       
  country.[64][65]                                                                                     
  Russia: Yandex is the leading search engine in Russia. As of December 2023, it accounted for at      
  least 63.8% of the market share.[66]                                                                 
  Multilingual SEO                                                                                     
  By the early 2000s, businesses recognized that the web and search engines could help them reach      
  global audiences. As a result, the need for multilingual SEO emerged.[67] In the early years of      
  international SEO development, simple translation was seen as sufficient. However, over time, it     
  became clear that localization and transcreation—adapting content to local language, culture, and    
  emotional resonance—were more effective than basic translation.[68]                                  
                                                                                                       
  Legal precedents                                                                                     
  On October 17, 2002, SearchKing filed suit in the United States District Court, Western District of  
  Oklahoma, against the search engine Google. SearchKing's claim was that Google's tactics to prevent  
  spamdexing constituted a tortious interference with contractual relations. On May 27, 2003, the      
  court granted Google's motion to dismiss the complaint because SearchKing "failed to state a claim   
  upon which relief may be granted."[69][70]                                                           
                                                                                                       
  In March 2006, KinderStart filed a lawsuit against Google over search engine rankings. KinderStart's 
   website was removed from Google's index prior to the lawsuit, and the amount of traffic to the site 
   dropped by 70%. On March 16, 2007, the United States District Court for the Northern District of    
  California (San Jose Division) dismissed KinderStart's complaint without leave to amend and          
  partially granted Google's motion for Rule 11 sanctions against KinderStart's attorney, requiring    
  him to pay part of Google's legal expenses.[71][72]

❯ I have vercel pro plan I am not worried about it. lets go     
  with A first, but is there anyway to build a combo of a and b 

● Yes, actually — and that's the smartest play. Next.js 14+ has
  what they call Partial Prerendering which basically gives you
  the best of both worlds:

  - Static pages (like About, Services, Legal) are pre-built at
  deploy time — zero JS, instant load, just like Astro
  - Dynamic pages (like the client portal, form submissions,
  GHL-connected features) use server-side rendering
  - API routes handle GHL integration securely on the backend

  So you get Astro's speed on content pages and Next.js's power
  on interactive pages. Same framework, no compromises.

  With your Vercel Pro plan you also get:
  - Analytics built in
  - Edge functions (GHL API calls from the closest server to the
   user)
  - Image optimization with no limits
  - Preview deployments for every git push
  - Custom domains with automatic SSL

  That's the approach then — Next.js with static generation
  where possible, SSR where needed, Tailwind CSS, Framer Motion
  for animations, and full i18n for English/Spanish.

  Let me move to the next question — design direction.

● Here's every single one of those broken down by what they
  actually do for you:

  Businesses

  - View/Edit Businesses — Read and update MED VEST's business
  info (name, address, hours) from your website or apps. Change
  business hours on the fly and it reflects everywhere.

  Calendars & Events

  - View/Edit Calendars — Create booking calendars ("Free
  Consultation", "Case Review", "Document Walkthrough")
  - View/Edit Calendar Events — Create, reschedule, cancel
  appointments programmatically. Client books on the website, it
   shows up here.
  - View/Edit Calendar Groups — Group multiple calendars
  together (e.g., round-robin between Shahpoor and a future
  employee)
  - View/Edit Calendar Resources — Manage rooms, Zoom links, or
  other resources tied to appointments

  Campaigns

  - View Campaigns — Pull campaign data (email blasts, SMS
  campaigns) to see performance — open rates, click rates, who
  engaged

  Conversations

  - View/Edit Conversations — The entire messaging hub. Every
  SMS, email, chat, Facebook DM, Instagram DM, WhatsApp message
  — all in one inbox. Read them, reply to them, all from the
  API.
  - View/Edit Conversation Messages — Send and read individual
  messages within conversations
  - View Conversation Reports — Analytics on response times,
  message volume, who's being responsive and who's ghosting
  - Livechat Typing Status — The chat widget on the website
  shows "typing..." when someone is responding. Makes it feel
  real-time and personal.

  Contacts (CRM)

  - View/Edit Contacts — The core of everything. Create contacts
   from website forms, update their info, add tags, add notes.
  Every person who touches MED VEST lives here. Search, filter,
  segment. "Show me all clients in the Documents Received stage
  who haven't uploaded anything in 7 days." Done.

  Objects & Associations

  - View/Edit Objects Schema — Custom objects beyond contacts
  and opportunities. Think "Cases", "Medical Providers",
  "Insurance Companies" as their own trackable things
  - View/Edit Objects Record — Create and manage records in
  those custom objects
  - View/Edit Associations — Link things together. Connect a
  client to their case, their insurance company, their attorney,
   their medical providers. Everything is related and
  searchable.

  Courses

  - View/Edit Courses — Build online courses or training.
  Shahpoor could create a "Client Guide to Medicare Set-Asides"
  course that new clients get access to automatically.
  Educational content that builds trust and reduces support
  questions.

  Forms

  - View/Edit Forms — Build and manage forms that replace
  Web3Forms. Contact forms, referral forms, intake
  questionnaires. Drag and drop builder. Conditional logic. File
   uploads. Every submission feeds directly into the CRM. This
  is what goes on the website.

  Invoices & Estimates

  - View/Edit Invoices — Send invoices to clients, track
  payments, see what's outstanding
  - View/Edit Invoice Schedules — Set up recurring invoices
  (monthly retainers, payment plans for MSA services)
  - View/Edit Invoice Templates — Branded invoice templates with
   MED VEST logo and colors
  - View/Edit Estimates — Send quotes/estimates before starting
  work. Client approves it, it converts to an invoice.

  Links

  - View/Edit Links — Trackable links. Create a link to share on
   social media or in emails and see exactly how many people
  clicked it, who they were, and what they did next.

  Email

  - View LC Email — Manage the built-in email system. Send from
  @medvst.com, track opens and clicks, maintain deliverability.

  Locations (Sub-Account Settings)

  - View Locations — Pull sub-account info
  - View/Edit Custom Values — Dynamic values like
  {{business.name}}, {{business.phone}} that auto-populate
  across emails, texts, forms. Change the phone number once, it
  updates everywhere.
  - View/Edit Custom Fields — Create fields specific to MED
  VEST: "Case Number", "Date of Injury", "Insurance Carrier",
  "Settlement Amount", "CMS Approval Status". These show up on
  contact records and forms.
  - View/Edit Tasks — Internal task management. "Call John back
  about his documents." "Follow up with Jane's insurance
  company." Assign tasks, set due dates, track completion.
  - View/Edit Recurring Tasks — Tasks that repeat. "Every
  Monday: review all cases in 'Pending Documents' stage."
  - View/Edit Tags — Tag contacts for segmentation. "Attorney
  Referral", "Self-Referred", "High Value", "Needs Follow-Up",
  "Case Complete". Then automate based on tags.
  - View Templates — Email and SMS templates. Pre-written
  messages for every scenario so Shahpoor doesn't have to type
  the same thing 50 times.

  Media

  - View/Edit Medias — Upload and manage images, documents,
  files within GHL. Client documents, marketing images, logo
  files — all stored and organized.

  Funnels & Pages

  - View Funnels/Pages/Redirects/Page Counts — GHL has a full
  page and funnel builder. You could build landing pages, opt-in
   pages, thank you pages — all tracked. "How many people
  visited the referral page vs. how many actually submitted?"
  Now you know.
  - Edit Redirect URLs — Set up redirects. Old medaside.com
  links can redirect to medvst.com pages.

  Opportunities (Pipeline)

  - View/Edit Opportunities — THIS IS THE MONEY. Create pipeline
   stages, move deals through them, assign values. Every case is
   an opportunity:
  New Inquiry ($0) → Intake Complete ($X) → MSA Drafting → CMS
  Submitted → Approved → Paid
  - Shahpoor opens his dashboard and sees $50K in his pipeline
  across 15 active cases. He's never had that visibility before.

  Payments

  - View/Edit Payment Orders — Process payments, view order
  history
  - Collect Payments — Actually charge cards. Clients can pay
  through the portal or through an invoice link.
  - View/Edit Payment Integrations — Connect Stripe, Square,
  PayPal — wherever Shahpoor wants to collect money
  - View Transactions — Full payment history. Who paid, when,
  how much, for what.
  - View Subscriptions — If Shahpoor offers payment plans, track
   recurring charges
  - View/Edit Coupons — Discount codes for promotions
  - View/Edit Custom Payment Providers — Connect niche payment
  processors if needed

  Products & Prices

  - View/Edit Products — Define Shahpoor's services as products:
   "MSA Administration - $X", "Lien Resolution - $X",
  "Settlement Consulting - $X"
  - View/Edit Product Prices — Set pricing, tiers, one-time vs
  recurring
  - View/Edit Product Collections — Bundle services together
  into packages

  SaaS Subscriptions

  - View/Edit SaaS Subscriptions — This is for YOUR agency.
  Manage sub-account billing. When you charge Shahpoor $397/mo,
  this is how you track and manage it.

  Social Media Planner

  - View/Edit Social Media Integrations — Connect Facebook,
  Instagram, Google Business Profile, LinkedIn, TikTok
  - View/Edit Social Media Posts — Create, schedule, publish
  posts across all platforms from one place. Write 20 posts on
  Sunday, schedule them for the month. Done.
  - View/Edit Social Media Accounts — Manage connected accounts
  - View/Edit Social Media CSV — Bulk upload posts via
  spreadsheet. Create a month of content in a CSV, upload it,
  done.
  - View/Edit Social Media Categories & Tags — Organize posts by
   category ("Client Testimonial", "Educational", "Company
  Update")
  - View Social Media Statistics — See what's performing. Which
  posts got engagement, which flopped. Data-driven social media.

  Store & Shipping

  - View/Edit Shipping — If MED VEST ever sells physical
  products or ships documents
  - View/Edit Store Settings — E-commerce settings. Probably not
   relevant now but it's there.

  Surveys

  - View Surveys — Create and manage surveys. Post-case
  satisfaction survey: "How was your experience with MED VEST?"
  Responses feed back into the CRM.

  Users

  - View/Edit Users — Manage who has access. Add Shahpoor as a
  user, give him a login. Add a future employee with limited
  permissions. Control who sees what.

  Workflows (Automations)

  - View Workflows — This is the brain of the entire system.
  Every automation lives here. "When form submitted → create
  contact → create opportunity → send text → send email → wait 2
   days → send follow-up." You build these once and they run
  forever. This is what makes the whole thing feel like magic.

  Email Builder

  - View/Edit Email Templates — Drag and drop email builder.
  Beautiful branded emails that look like MED VEST hired a
  design team. Welcome emails, follow-ups, newsletters, case
  updates.
  - View/Edit Email Schedules — Schedule emails in advance.
  Campaign going out next Tuesday? Set it and forget it.

  Blogs & WordPress

  - View WordPress Site — Connect to a WordPress blog if needed
  - Create/Update Blog Posts — Publish content for SEO. "What is
   a Medicare Set-Aside?" articles that drive organic traffic
  - View Blog Categories/Authors — Organize content

  Brand Boards

  - View/Edit Design Kit — Store MED VEST brand colors, fonts,
  logos in one place. Every email, form, and page automatically
  pulls from this so everything looks consistent.
