❯ Hold oon what is pulling the data? GHL is pulling it from my  
  website?                                                      

● Other way around.

  Your website pushes data TO GHL.

  When someone fills out a form on medvst.com, the website sends
   that data to GHL through the API. GHL stores it, creates the
  contact, triggers the automations.

  Think of it like this:

  - Your website = the front door (what clients see and interact
   with)
  - GHL = the back office (where everything gets processed,
  stored, and automated)
  - The API key = the connection between them

  So when a client fills out the referral form on your site, the
   website says "hey GHL, here's a new person — name, email,
  phone, case details" and GHL takes it from there. Creates the
  contact, puts them in the pipeline, fires off the welcome
  text, sends the email, notifies Shahpoor.

  GHL doesn't pull anything on its own. Your website sends it.
  That's what I'm going to build — I'm replacing the Web3Forms
  code with GHL API calls so everything flows into his CRM
  instead of just landing in an email inbox.

  Make sense? Go grab that key.

  It's safe to proceed. This is YOUR private integration for
  YOUR sub-account. Nobody else has this key — it's only going
  to be used in the website code that you control.

❯ Search engine optimization (SEO) is the practice of improving the visibility and overall performance 
   of websites and web pages in search engine results pages (SERPs).[1] It focuses on increasing the   
  quantity and quality of traffic from unpaid (organic) search results rather than paid                
  advertising.[2] SEO applies to multiple search formats, including web, image, video, news, academic, 
   and vertical search engines, as well as AI-assisted search interfaces.                              
                                                                                                       
  SEO is commonly used as part of a broader digital marketing strategy and involves optimizing         
  technical infrastructure, content relevance, and authority signals to improve rankings for user      
  queries.[3] The objective of SEO is to attract users who are actively searching for information,     
  products, or services, thereby improving brand visibility, user engagement, and conversions.[4]      
                                                                                                       
  History                                                                                              
  Webmasters and content providers began optimizing websites for search engines in the mid-1990s as    
  the first search engines were cataloging the early Web. Search engine users would query the URL of a 
   page, and then receive information found on the page, if it existed in the search engine's index.   
                                                                                                       
  ALIWEB and the earliest versions of search engines required website developers to manually upload    
  website index files in order to be searchable and widely did not utilize any form of ranking         
  algorithm for user queries.[1] The emergence of automated web crawlers would later be used to        
  proactively discover and index websites. This led to website developers to optimize their website’s  
  search signals, including the use of meta tags, to achieve greater visibility in search results.     
                                                                                                       
  According to a 2004 article by former industry analyst and current Google employee Danny Sullivan,   
  the phrase "search engine optimization" came into use in 1997. Sullivan credits SEO practitioner     
  Bruce Clay as one of the first people to popularize the term.[5]                                     
                                                                                                       
  In some cases, early search algorithms weighted particular HTML attributes in ways that could be     
  leveraged by web content providers to manipulate their search rankings.[6] As early as 1997, search  
  engine providers began adjusting their algorithms to prevent these actions.[3] Eventually, search    
  engines would incorporate more meaningful measures of page purpose, including the more recent        
  development of semantic search.[7]                                                                   
                                                                                                       
  Some search engines frequently sponsor SEO conferences, webchats, and seminars. Major search engines 
   provide information and guidelines to help with website optimization.[8][4] Google                  
  … +70 lines …                                                                                        
  ain (ccTLD) or a relevant top-level domain (TLD) for the target market, choosing web hosting with a  
  local IP address or server, and using a Content Delivery Network (CDN) to improve website speed and  
  performance globally. It is also important to understand the local culture so that the content feels 
   relevant to the audience. This includes conducting keyword research for each market, using hreflang 
   tags to target the right languages, and building local backlinks. However, the core SEO             
  principles—such as creating high-quality content, improving user experience, and building            
  links—remain the same, regardless of language or region.[60]                                         
                                                                                                       
  Regional search engines have a strong presence in specific markets:                                  
                                                                                                       
  China: Baidu leads the market, controlling about 70 to 80% market share.[63]                         
  South Korea: Since the end of 2021, Naver, a domestic web portal, has gained prominence in the       
  country.[64][65]                                                                                     
  Russia: Yandex is the leading search engine in Russia. As of December 2023, it accounted for at      
  least 63.8% of the market share.[66]                                                                 
  Multilingual SEO                                                                                     
  By the early 2000s, businesses recognized that the web and search engines could help them reach      
  global audiences. As a result, the need for multilingual SEO emerged.[67] In the early years of      
  international SEO development, simple translation was seen as sufficient. However, over time, it     
  became clear that localization and transcreation—adapting content to local language, culture, and    
  emotional resonance—were more effective than basic translation.[68]                                  
                                                                                                       
  Legal precedents                                                                                     
  On October 17, 2002, SearchKing filed suit in the United States District Court, Western District of  
  Oklahoma, against the search engine Google. SearchKing's claim was that Google's tactics to prevent  
  spamdexing constituted a tortious interference with contractual relations. On May 27, 2003, the      
  court granted Google's motion to dismiss the complaint because SearchKing "failed to state a claim   
  upon which relief may be granted."[69][70]                                                           
                                                                                                       
  In March 2006, KinderStart filed a lawsuit against Google over search engine rankings. KinderStart's 
   website was removed from Google's index prior to the lawsuit, and the amount of traffic to the site 
   dropped by 70%. On March 16, 2007, the United States District Court for the Northern District of    
  California (San Jose Division) dismissed KinderStart's complaint without leave to amend and          
  partially granted Google's motion for Rule 11 sanctions against KinderStart's attorney, requiring    
  him to pay part of Google's legal expenses.[71][72]

❯ I have vercel pro plan I am not worried about it. lets go     
  with A first, but is there anyway to build a combo of a and b 

● Yes, actually — and that's the smartest play. Next.js 14+ has
  what they call Partial Prerendering which basically gives you
  the best of both worlds:

  - Static pages (like About, Services, Legal) are pre-built at
  deploy time — zero JS, instant load, just like Astro
  - Dynamic pages (like the client portal, form submissions,
  GHL-connected features) use server-side rendering
  - API routes handle GHL integration securely on the backend

  So you get Astro's speed on content pages and Next.js's power
  on interactive pages. Same framework, no compromises.

  With your Vercel Pro plan you also get:
  - Analytics built in
  - Edge functions (GHL API calls from the closest server to the
   user)
  - Image optimization with no limits
  - Preview deployments for every git push
  - Custom domains with automatic SSL

  That's the approach then — Next.js with static generation
  where possible, SSR where needed, Tailwind CSS, Framer Motion
  for animations, and full i18n for English/Spanish.

  Let me move to the next question — design direction.

● Here's every single one of those broken down by what they
  actually do for you:

  Businesses

  - View/Edit Businesses — Read and update MED VEST's business
  info (name, address, hours) from your website or apps. Change
  business hours on the fly and it reflects everywhere.

  Calendars & Events

  - View/Edit Calendars — Create booking calendars ("Free
  Consultation", "Case Review", "Document Walkthrough")
  - View/Edit Calendar Events — Create, reschedule, cancel
  appointments programmatically. Client books on the website, it
   shows up here.
  - View/Edit Calendar Groups — Group multiple calendars
  together (e.g., round-robin between Shahpoor and a future
  employee)
  - View/Edit Calendar Resources — Manage rooms, Zoom links, or
  other resources tied to appointments

  Campaigns

  - View Campaigns — Pull campaign data (email blasts, SMS
  campaigns) to see performance — open rates, click rates, who
  engaged

  Conversations

  - View/Edit Conversations — The entire messaging hub. Every
  SMS, email, chat, Facebook DM, Instagram DM, WhatsApp message
  — all in one inbox. Read them, reply to them, all from the
  API.
  - View/Edit Conversation Messages — Send and read individual
  messages within conversations
  - View Conversation Reports — Analytics on response times,
  message volume, who's being responsive and who's ghosting
  - Livechat Typing Status — The chat widget on the website
  shows "typing..." when someone is responding. Makes it feel
  real-time and personal.

  Contacts (CRM)

  - View/Edit Contacts — The core of everything. Create contacts
   from website forms, update their info, add tags, add notes.
  Every person who touches MED VEST lives here. Search, filter,
  segment. "Show me all clients in the Documents Received stage
  who haven't uploaded anything in 7 days." Done.

  Objects & Associations

  - View/Edit Objects Schema — Custom objects beyond contacts
  and opportunities. Think "Cases", "Medical Providers",
  "Insurance Companies" as their own trackable things
  - View/Edit Objects Record — Create and manage records in
  those custom objects
  - View/Edit Associations — Link things together. Connect a
  client to their case, their insurance company, their attorney,
   their medical providers. Everything is related and
  searchable.

  Courses

  - View/Edit Courses — Build online courses or training.
  Shahpoor could create a "Client Guide to Medicare Set-Asides"
  course that new clients get access to automatically.
  Educational content that builds trust and reduces support
  questions.

  Forms

  - View/Edit Forms — Build and manage forms that replace
  Web3Forms. Contact forms, referral forms, intake
  questionnaires. Drag and drop builder. Conditional logic. File
   uploads. Every submission feeds directly into the CRM. This
  is what goes on the website.

  Invoices & Estimates

  - View/Edit Invoices — Send invoices to clients, track
  payments, see what's outstanding
  - View/Edit Invoice Schedules — Set up recurring invoices
  (monthly retainers, payment plans for MSA services)
  - View/Edit Invoice Templates — Branded invoice templates with
   MED VEST logo and colors
  - View/Edit Estimates — Send quotes/estimates before starting
  work. Client approves it, it converts to an invoice.

  Links

  - View/Edit Links — Trackable links. Create a link to share on
   social media or in emails and see exactly how many people
  clicked it, who they were, and what they did next.

  Email

  - View LC Email — Manage the built-in email system. Send from
  @medvst.com, track opens and clicks, maintain deliverability.

  Locations (Sub-Account Settings)

  - View Locations — Pull sub-account info
  - View/Edit Custom Values — Dynamic values like
  {{business.name}}, {{business.phone}} that auto-populate
  across emails, texts, forms. Change the phone number once, it
  updates everywhere.
  - View/Edit Custom Fields — Create fields specific to MED
  VEST: "Case Number", "Date of Injury", "Insurance Carrier",
  "Settlement Amount", "CMS Approval Status". These show up on
  contact records and forms.
  - View/Edit Tasks — Internal task management. "Call John back
  about his documents." "Follow up with Jane's insurance
  company." Assign tasks, set due dates, track completion.
  - View/Edit Recurring Tasks — Tasks that repeat. "Every
  Monday: review all cases in 'Pending Documents' stage."
  - View/Edit Tags — Tag contacts for segmentation. "Attorney
  Referral", "Self-Referred", "High Value", "Needs Follow-Up",
  "Case Complete". Then automate based on tags.
  - View Templates — Email and SMS templates. Pre-written
  messages for every scenario so Shahpoor doesn't have to type
  the same thing 50 times.

  Media

  - View/Edit Medias — Upload and manage images, documents,
  files within GHL. Client documents, marketing images, logo
  files — all stored and organized.

  Funnels & Pages

  - View Funnels/Pages/Redirects/Page Counts — GHL has a full
  page and funnel builder. You could build landing pages, opt-in
   pages, thank you pages — all tracked. "How many people
  visited the referral page vs. how many actually submitted?"
  Now you know.
  - Edit Redirect URLs — Set up redirects. Old medaside.com
  links can redirect to medvst.com pages.

  Opportunities (Pipeline)

  - View/Edit Opportunities — THIS IS THE MONEY. Create pipeline
   stages, move deals through them, assign values. Every case is
   an opportunity:
  New Inquiry ($0) → Intake Complete ($X) → MSA Drafting → CMS
  Submitted → Approved → Paid
  - Shahpoor opens his dashboard and sees $50K in his pipeline
  across 15 active cases. He's never had that visibility before.

  Payments

  - View/Edit Payment Orders — Process payments, view order
  history
  - Collect Payments — Actually charge cards. Clients can pay
  through the portal or through an invoice link.
  - View/Edit Payment Integrations — Connect Stripe, Square,
  PayPal — wherever Shahpoor wants to collect money
  - View Transactions — Full payment history. Who paid, when,
  how much, for what.
  - View Subscriptions — If Shahpoor offers payment plans, track
   recurring charges
  - View/Edit Coupons — Discount codes for promotions
  - View/Edit Custom Payment Providers — Connect niche payment

  Products & Prices

   "MSA Administration - $X", "Lien Resolution - $X",

  - View/Edit Product Collections — Bundle services together

  SaaS Subscriptions

  this is how you track and manage it.

  Social Media Planner

  Store & Shipping

  - View/Edit Store Settings — E-commerce settings. Probably not

  permissions. Control who sees what.

  Workflows (Automations)

  Every automation lives here. "When form submitted → create
  contact → create opportunity → send text → send email → wait 2

  forever. This is what makes the whole thing feel like magic.

  Email Builder

  Blogs & WordPress

  - Create/Update Blog Posts — Publish content for SEO. "What is

  Charges

  level

  Documents & Contracts

  - View Document/Contract List — Digital contracts and

  - Send Document/Contract Links — Send a contract to a client,

  Voice AI

✻ Cogitated for 1m 21s

❯ Hold oon what is pulling the data? GHL is pulling it from my  
  website?                                                      

● Other way around.

  Your website pushes data TO GHL.

  When someone fills out a form on medvst.com, the website sends
   that data to GHL through the API. GHL stores it, creates the
  contact, triggers the automations.

  Think of it like this:

  - Your website = the front door (what clients see and interact
   with)
  - GHL = the back office (where everything gets processed,
  stored, and automated)
  - The API key = the connection between them

  So when a client fills out the referral form on your site, the
   website says "hey GHL, here's a new person — name, email,
  phone, case details" and GHL takes it from there. Creates the
  contact, puts them in the pipeline, fires off the welcome
  text, sends the email, notifies Shahpoor.

  GHL doesn't pull anything on its own. Your website sends it.
  That's what I'm going to build — I'm replacing the Web3Forms
  code with GHL API calls so everything flows into his CRM
  instead of just landing in an email inbox.

  Make sense? Go grab that key.

❯ Security Risk                                                 
                                                                
  Are you sure you want to proceed with creating the private    
  integration token with sensitive scopes? What are the         
  sensitive scopes?                                             

● That's just a standard warning because you selected all
  scopes. The "sensitive" ones are probably:

  - Payments — can process charges
  - Phone numbers — can buy/manage numbers (costs money)
  - Users — can add/remove people with access
  - Conversations — can send messages on your behalf
  - Contacts — can read/modify client data

  It's safe to proceed. This is YOUR private integration for
  YOUR sub-account. Nobody else has this key — it's only going
  to be used in the website code that you control.

  Hit Yes / Proceed and grab the key.

❯ For shapoor                                                   

● Right — Shahpoor's sub-account that YOU manage. You own the

❯ Search engine optimization (SEO) is the practice of improving the visibility and overall  
  performance of websites and web pages in search engine results pages (SERPs).[1] It       
  focuses on increasing the quantity and quality of traffic from unpaid (organic) search    
  results rather than paid advertising.[2] SEO applies to multiple search formats,          
  including web, image, video, news, academic, and vertical search engines, as well as      
  AI-assisted search interfaces.                                                            
                                                                                            
  SEO is commonly used as part of a broader digital marketing strategy and involves         
  optimizing technical infrastructure, content relevance, and authority signals to improve  
  rankings for user queries.[3] The objective of SEO is to attract users who are actively   
  searching for information, products, or services, thereby improving brand visibility,     
  user engagement, and conversions.[4]                                                      
                                                                                            
  History                                                                                   
  Webmasters and content providers began optimizing websites for search engines in the      
  mid-1990s as the first search engines were cataloging the early Web. Search engine users  
  would query the URL of a page, and then receive information found on the page, if it      
  existed in the search engine's index.                                                     
                                                                                            
  ALIWEB and the earliest versions of search engines required website developers to         
  manually upload website index files in order to be searchable and widely did not utilize  
  any form of ranking algorithm for user queries.[1] The emergence of automated web         
  crawlers would later be used to proactively discover and index websites. This led to      
  website developers to optimize their website’s search signals, including the use of meta  
  tags, to achieve greater visibility in search results.                                    
                                                                                            
  According to a 2004 article by former industry analyst and current Google employee Danny  
  Sullivan, the phrase "search engine optimization" came into use in 1997. Sullivan credits 
   SEO practitioner Bruce Clay as one of the first people to popularize the term.[5]        
                                                                                            
  In some cases, early search algorithms weighted particular HTML attributes in ways that   
  could be leveraged by web content providers to manipulate their search rankings.[6] As    
  early as 1997, search engine providers began adjusting their algorithms to prevent these  
  actions.[3] Eventually, search engines would incorporate more meaningful measures of page 
   purpose, including the more recent development of semantic search.[7]                    
                                                                                            
  Some search engines frequently sponsor SEO conferences, webchats, and seminars. Major     
  search engines provide information and guidelines to help with website                    
  optimization.[8][4] Google                                                                
  … +70 lines …                                                                             
  ain (ccTLD) or a relevant top-level domain (TLD) for the target market, choosing web      
  hosting with a local IP address or server, and using a Content Delivery Network (CDN) to  
  improve website speed and performance globally. It is also important to understand the    
  local culture so that the content feels relevant to the audience. This includes           
  conducting keyword research for each market, using hreflang tags to target the right      
  languages, and building local backlinks. However, the core SEO principles—such as         
  creating high-quality content, improving user experience, and building links—remain the   
  same, regardless of language or region.[60]                                               
                                                                                            
  Regional search engines have a strong presence in specific markets:                       
                                                                                            
  China: Baidu leads the market, controlling about 70 to 80% market share.[63]              
  South Korea: Since the end of 2021, Naver, a domestic web portal, has gained prominence   
  in the country.[64][65]                                                                   
  Russia: Yandex is the leading search engine in Russia. As of December 2023, it accounted  
  for at least 63.8% of the market share.[66]                                               
  Multilingual SEO                                                                          
  By the early 2000s, businesses recognized that the web and search engines could help them 
   reach global audiences. As a result, the need for multilingual SEO emerged.[67] In the   
  early years of international SEO development, simple translation was seen as sufficient.  
  However, over time, it became clear that localization and transcreation—adapting content  
  to local language, culture, and emotional resonance—were more effective than basic        
  translation.[68]                                                                          
                                                                                            
  Legal precedents                                                                          
  On October 17, 2002, SearchKing filed suit in the United States District Court, Western   
  District of Oklahoma, against the search engine Google. SearchKing's claim was that       
  Google's tactics to prevent spamdexing constituted a tortious interference with           
  contractual relations. On May 27, 2003, the court granted Google's motion to dismiss the  
  complaint because SearchKing "failed to state a claim upon which relief may be            
  granted."[69][70]                                                                         
                                                                                            
  In March 2006, KinderStart filed a lawsuit against Google over search engine rankings.    
  KinderStart's website was removed from Google's index prior to the lawsuit, and the       
  amount of traffic to the site dropped by 70%. On March 16, 2007, the United States        
  District Court for the Northern District of California (San Jose Division) dismissed      
  KinderStart's complaint without leave to amend and partially granted Google's motion for  
  Rule 11 sanctions against KinderStart's attorney, requiring him to pay part of Google's   
  legal expenses.[71][72]

❯ I have vercel pro plan I am not worried about it. lets go     
  with A first, but is there anyway to build a combo of a and b 

● Yes, actually — and that's the smartest play. Next.js 14+ has
  what they call Partial Prerendering which basically gives you
  the best of both worlds:

  - Static pages (like About, Services, Legal) are pre-built at
  deploy time — zero JS, instant load, just like Astro
  - Dynamic pages (like the client portal, form submissions,
  GHL-connected features) use server-side rendering
  - API routes handle GHL integration securely on the backend

  So you get Astro's speed on content pages and Next.js's power
  on interactive pages. Same framework, no compromises.

  With your Vercel Pro plan you also get:
  - Analytics built in
  - Edge functions (GHL API calls from the closest server to the
   user)
  - Image optimization with no limits
  - Preview deployments for every git push
  - Custom domains with automatic SSL

  That's the approach then — Next.js with static generation
  where possible, SSR where needed, Tailwind CSS, Framer Motion
  for animations, and full i18n for English/Spanish.

  Let me move to the next question — design direction.

● Here's every single one of those broken down by what they
  actually do for you:

  Businesses

  - View/Edit Businesses — Read and update MED VEST's business
  info (name, address, hours) from your website or apps. Change
  business hours on the fly and it reflects everywhere.

  Calendars & Events

  - View/Edit Calendars — Create booking calendars ("Free
  Consultation", "Case Review", "Document Walkthrough")
  - View/Edit Calendar Events — Create, reschedule, cancel
  appointments programmatically. Client books on the website, it
   shows up here.
  - View/Edit Calendar Groups — Group multiple calendars
  together (e.g., round-robin between Shahpoor and a future
  employee)
  - View/Edit Calendar Resources — Manage rooms, Zoom links, or
  other resources tied to appointments

  Campaigns

  - View Campaigns — Pull campaign data (email blasts, SMS
  campaigns) to see performance — open rates, click rates, who
  engaged

  Conversations

  - View/Edit Conversations — The entire messaging hub. Every
  SMS, email, chat, Facebook DM, Instagram DM, WhatsApp message
  — all in one inbox. Read them, reply to them, all from the
  API.
  - View/Edit Conversation Messages — Send and read individual
  messages within conversations
  - View Conversation Reports — Analytics on response times,
  message volume, who's being responsive and who's ghosting
  - Livechat Typing Status — The chat widget on the website
  shows "typing..." when someone is responding. Makes it feel
  real-time and personal.

  Contacts (CRM)

  - View/Edit Contacts — The core of everything. Create contacts
   from website forms, update their info, add tags, add notes.
  Every person who touches MED VEST lives here. Search, filter,
  segment. "Show me all clients in the Documents Received stage
  who haven't uploaded anything in 7 days." Done.

  Objects & Associations

  - View/Edit Objects Schema — Custom objects beyond contacts
  and opportunities. Think "Cases", "Medical Providers",
  "Insurance Companies" as their own trackable things
  - View/Edit Objects Record — Create and manage records in
  those custom objects
  - View/Edit Associations — Link things together. Connect a
  client to their case, their insurance company, their attorney,
   their medical providers. Everything is related and
  searchable.

  Courses

  - View/Edit Courses — Build online courses or training.
  Shahpoor could create a "Client Guide to Medicare Set-Asides"
  course that new clients get access to automatically.
  Educational content that builds trust and reduces support
  questions.

  Forms

  - View/Edit Forms — Build and manage forms that replace
  Web3Forms. Contact forms, referral forms, intake
  questionnaires. Drag and drop builder. Conditional logic. File
   uploads. Every submission feeds directly into the CRM. This
  is what goes on the website.

  Invoices & Estimates

  - View/Edit Invoices — Send invoices to clients, track
  payments, see what's outstanding
  - View/Edit Invoice Schedules — Set up recurring invoices
  (monthly retainers, payment plans for MSA services)
  - View/Edit Invoice Templates — Branded invoice templates with
   MED VEST logo and colors
  - View/Edit Estimates — Send quotes/estimates before starting
  work. Client approves it, it converts to an invoice.

  Links

  - View/Edit Links — Trackable links. Create a link to share on
   social media or in emails and see exactly how many people
  clicked it, who they were, and what they did next.

  Email

  - View LC Email — Manage the built-in email system. Send from
  @medvst.com, track opens and clicks, maintain deliverability.

  Locations (Sub-Account Settings)

  - View Locations — Pull sub-account info
  - View/Edit Custom Values — Dynamic values like
  {{business.name}}, {{business.phone}} that auto-populate
  across emails, texts, forms. Change the phone number once, it
  updates everywhere.
  - View/Edit Custom Fields — Create fields specific to MED
  VEST: "Case Number", "Date of Injury", "Insurance Carrier",
  "Settlement Amount", "CMS Approval Status". These show up on
  contact records and forms.
  - View/Edit Tasks — Internal task management. "Call John back
  about his documents." "Follow up with Jane's insurance
  company." Assign tasks, set due dates, track completion.
  - View/Edit Recurring Tasks — Tasks that repeat. "Every
  Monday: review all cases in 'Pending Documents' stage."
  - View/Edit Tags — Tag contacts for segmentation. "Attorney
  Referral", "Self-Referred", "High Value", "Needs Follow-Up",
  "Case Complete". Then automate based on tags.
  - View Templates — Email and SMS templates. Pre-written
  messages for every scenario so Shahpoor doesn't have to type
  the same thing 50 times.

  Media

  - View/Edit Medias — Upload and manage images, documents,
  files within GHL. Client documents, marketing images, logo
  files — all stored and organized.

  Funnels & Pages

  - View Funnels/Pages/Redirects/Page Counts — GHL has a full

❯ Hold oon what is pulling the data? GHL is pulling it from my  
  website?                                                      

● Other way around.

  Your website pushes data TO GHL.

  When someone fills out a form on medvst.com, the website sends
   that data to GHL through the API. GHL stores it, creates the
  contact, triggers the automations.

  Think of it like this:

  - Your website = the front door (what clients see and interact
   with)
  - GHL = the back office (where everything gets processed,
  stored, and automated)
  - The API key = the connection between them

  So when a client fills out the referral form on your site, the
   website says "hey GHL, here's a new person — name, email,
  phone, case details" and GHL takes it from there. Creates the
  contact, puts them in the pipeline, fires off the welcome
  text, sends the email, notifies Shahpoor.

  GHL doesn't pull anything on its own. Your website sends it.
  That's what I'm going to build — I'm replacing the Web3Forms
  code with GHL API calls so everything flows into his CRM
  instead of just landing in an email inbox.

  Make sense? Go grab that key.

❯ Security Risk                                                 
                                                                
  Are you sure you want to proceed with creating the private    
  integration token with sensitive scopes? What are the

● That's just a standard warning because you selected all
  scopes. The "sensitive" ones are probably:

  - Payments — can process charges
  - Phone numbers — can buy/manage numbers (costs money)
  - Users — can add/remove people with access
  - Conversations — can send messages on your behalf
  - Contacts — can read/modify client data

  It's safe to proceed. This is YOUR private integration for
  YOUR sub-account. Nobody else has this key — it's only going
  to be used in the website code that you control.

  Hit Yes / Proceed and grab the key.

❯ Search engine optimization (SEO) is the practice of improving the visibility and overall        
  performance of websites and web pages in search engine results pages (SERPs).[1] It focuses on  
  increasing the quantity and quality of traffic from unpaid (organic) search results rather than 
   paid advertising.[2] SEO applies to multiple search formats, including web, image, video,      
  news, academic, and vertical search engines, as well as AI-assisted search interfaces.          
                                                                                                  
  SEO is commonly used as part of a broader digital marketing strategy and involves optimizing    
  technical infrastructure, content relevance, and authority signals to improve rankings for user 
   queries.[3] The objective of SEO is to attract users who are actively searching for            
  information, products, or services, thereby improving brand visibility, user engagement, and    
  conversions.[4]                                                                                 
                                                                                                  
  History                                                                                         
  Webmasters and content providers began optimizing websites for search engines in the mid-1990s  
  as the first search engines were cataloging the early Web. Search engine users would query the  
  URL of a page, and then receive information found on the page, if it existed in the search      
  engine's index.                                                                                 
                                                                                                  
  ALIWEB and the earliest versions of search engines required website developers to manually      
  upload website index files in order to be searchable and widely did not utilize any form of     
  ranking algorithm for user queries.[1] The emergence of automated web crawlers would later be   
  used to proactively discover and index websites. This led to website developers to optimize     
  their website’s search signals, including the use of meta tags, to achieve greater visibility   
  in search results.                                                                              
                                                                                                  
  According to a 2004 article by former industry analyst and current Google employee Danny        
  Sullivan, the phrase "search engine optimization" came into use in 1997. Sullivan credits SEO   
  practitioner Bruce Clay as one of the first people to popularize the term.[5]                   
                                                                                                  
  In some cases, early search algorithms weighted particular HTML attributes in ways that could   
  be leveraged by web content providers to manipulate their search rankings.[6] As early as 1997, 
   search engine providers began adjusting their algorithms to prevent these actions.[3]          
  Eventually, search engines would incorporate more meaningful measures of page purpose,          
  including the more recent development of semantic search.[7]                                    
                                                                                                  
  Some search engines frequently sponsor SEO conferences, webchats, and seminars. Major search    
  engines provide information and guidelines to help with website optimization.[8][4] Google      
  … +70 lines …                                                                                   
  ain (ccTLD) or a relevant top-level domain (TLD) for the target market, choosing web hosting    
  with a local IP address or server, and using a Content Delivery Network (CDN) to improve        
  website speed and performance globally. It is also important to understand the local culture so 
   that the content feels relevant to the audience. This includes conducting keyword research for 
   each market, using hreflang tags to target the right languages, and building local backlinks.  
  However, the core SEO principles—such as creating high-quality content, improving user          
  experience, and building links—remain the same, regardless of language or region.[60]           
                                                                                                  
  Regional search engines have a strong presence in specific markets:                             
                                                                                                  
  China: Baidu leads the market, controlling about 70 to 80% market share.[63]                    
  South Korea: Since the end of 2021, Naver, a domestic web portal, has gained prominence in the  
  country.[64][65]                                                                                
  Russia: Yandex is the leading search engine in Russia. As of December 2023, it accounted for at 
   least 63.8% of the market share.[66]                                                           
  Multilingual SEO                                                                                
  By the early 2000s, businesses recognized that the web and search engines could help them reach 
   global audiences. As a result, the need for multilingual SEO emerged.[67] In the early years   
  of international SEO development, simple translation was seen as sufficient. However, over      
  time, it became clear that localization and transcreation—adapting content to local language,   
  culture, and emotional resonance—were more effective than basic translation.[68]                
                                                                                                  
  Legal precedents                                                                                
  On October 17, 2002, SearchKing filed suit in the United States District Court, Western         
  District of Oklahoma, against the search engine Google. SearchKing's claim was that Google's    
  tactics to prevent spamdexing constituted a tortious interference with contractual relations.   
  On May 27, 2003, the court granted Google's motion to dismiss the complaint because SearchKing  
  "failed to state a claim upon which relief may be granted."[69][70]                             
                                                                                                  
  In March 2006, KinderStart filed a lawsuit against Google over search engine rankings.          
  KinderStart's website was removed from Google's index prior to the lawsuit, and the amount of   
  traffic to the site dropped by 70%. On March 16, 2007, the United States District Court for the 
   Northern District of California (San Jose Division) dismissed KinderStart's complaint without  
  leave to amend and partially granted Google's motion for Rule 11 sanctions against              
  KinderStart's attorney, requiring him to pay part of Google's legal expenses.[71][72]

❯ I have vercel pro plan I am not worried about it. lets go     
  with A first, but is there anyway to build a combo of a and b 

● Yes, actually — and that's the smartest play. Next.js 14+ has
  what they call Partial Prerendering which basically gives you
  the best of both worlds:

  - Static pages (like About, Services, Legal) are pre-built at
  deploy time — zero JS, instant load, just like Astro
  - Dynamic pages (like the client portal, form submissions,
  GHL-connected features) use server-side rendering
  - API routes handle GHL integration securely on the backend

  So you get Astro's speed on content pages and Next.js's power
  on interactive pages. Same framework, no compromises.

  With your Vercel Pro plan you also get:
  - Analytics built in
  - Edge functions (GHL API calls from the closest server to the
   user)
  - Image optimization with no limits
  - Preview deployments for every git push
  - Custom domains with automatic SSL

  That's the approach then — Next.js with static generation
  where possible, SSR where needed, Tailwind CSS, Framer Motion
  for animations, and full i18n for English/Spanish.

  Let me move to the next question — design direction.

● Got it — English + Spanish, not Farsi. That's actually simpler
   (no RTL layout needed).

  Next.js has built-in i18n routing that handles this cleanly —
  /en/services and /es/services with automatic locale detection.
   Google indexes both versions separately, which doubles your
  SEO surface area.

  Take a look at the tech stack options in the browser at

  want to go. Or if you're good with my recommendation (Option A
   - Next.js), just say the word and I'll move to the next
  question.

❯ I have vercel pro plan I am not worried about it. lets go     
  with A first, but is there anyway to build a combo of a and b 

● Yes, actually — and that's the smartest play. Next.js 14+ has
  what they call Partial Prerendering which basically gives you
  the best of both worlds:

  - Static pages (like About, Services, Legal) are pre-built at
  deploy time — zero JS, instant load, just like Astro
  - Dynamic pages (like the client portal, form submissions,
  GHL-connected features) use server-side rendering
  - API routes handle GHL integration securely on the backend

  So you get Astro's speed on content pages and Next.js's power
  on interactive pages. Same framework, no compromises.

  With your Vercel Pro plan you also get:
  - Analytics built in
  - Edge functions (GHL API calls from the closest server to the
   user)
  - Image optimization with no limits
  - Preview deployments for every git push
  - Custom domains with automatic SSL

  That's the approach then — Next.js with static generation
  where possible, SSR where needed, Tailwind CSS, Framer Motion
  for animations, and full i18n for English/Spanish.

  Let me move to the next question — design direction.

  ---                                                                                             
  MED VEST — Full Site Build Documentation                                                        
                                                                                                  
  Project Overview                             
                                                                                                  
  What this is: A complete website rebuild for MED VEST (medvst.com), a Medicare Set-Aside (MSA) 
  administration company owned by Shahpoor, based in Van Nuys, CA. This is a ground-up rebuild    
  from a static HTML/CSS site (previously called "MED ASIDE") into a modern full-stack Next.js    
  application.                                                                                    
                                                                                                  
  Who built it: Brandon Bible / Adaptation Living LLC (info@adaptationliving.com)                 
                                                                                   
  Why it exists: Shahpoor's business helps injured people (claimants) navigate Medicare Set-Aside 
  administration, lien resolution, settlement consulting, and trust services. The old site was
  static HTML with disconnected tools (Web3Forms, Cloudinary, Tawk.to). This rebuild integrates   
  everything through GoHighLevel (GHL) CRM and delivers an enterprise-grade, bilingual,           
  SEO-optimized site designed to convert visitors into clients.
                                                                                                  
  ---                                                                              
  Business Context  
                                                                                                  
  Client Details                               
                                                                                                  
  - Business Name: MED VEST (rebranded from MED ASIDE)                             
  - Owner: Shahpoor                                                                               
  - Domain: medvst.com (purchased through Namecheap via Google, not yet linked to Brandon's
  account)                                     
  - Address: PO Box 8294, Van Nuys, CA 91410              
  - Phone: (818) 674-1211                                 
  - Email: info@medvst.com                     
  - Target Audience: Injured parties / claimants and their families (regular people, NOT          
  attorneys)                                              
  - Services: MSA Administration, Lien Resolution, Settlement Consulting, Trust Services,         
  Liability Settlements                                                            
  - Service Area: All 50 states                
                                                                                                  
  Agency Details                                                                                  
                                                                                                  
  - Agency: Adaptation Living LLC (Brandon Bible)                                                 
  - GoHighLevel: Brandon has an agency-level GHL subscription. Shahpoor's business is set up as a 
  sub-account.                                                                                    
  - Pricing Model: Brandon plans to charge Shahpoor ~$397-497/mo for the GHL-powered system +     
  $1,000-1,500 setup fee.                                                          
  - Second Site: Shahpoor also has medaside.com — that site will be fixed later, separate project.
                                                                                   
  GoHighLevel Integration Details                                                                 
                                                                                   
  - GHL Location ID: ABxgFApScndDJpUIDcl9                                                         
  - GHL API Key: pit-9cb5efeb-8294-4cee-a0c2-ff8d65c73cc4 (store as env var, NEVER expose         
  client-side)                                            
  - GHL Sub-Account URL: https://app.gohighlevel.com/v2/location/ABxgFApScndDJpUIDcl9/dashboard   
  - What GHL replaces:                                                             
    - Web3Forms → GHL Forms (contact + referral/case intake)                                      
    - Cloudinary → GHL File Upload (document intake)                               
    - Tawk.to → GHL Chat Widget                                                                   
    - No CRM → GHL CRM + Pipeline                                                                 
    - Dead portal page → GHL Client Portal (real login, case tracking)                            
    - Nothing → GHL Booking Calendar, SMS/Email automations, phone system                         
  - API Architecture: All GHL API calls go through Next.js API routes (/api/ghl/*). The API key is
   stored as GHL_API_KEY env var on Vercel. Client-side code NEVER touches the key.               
                                                                                   
  Previous Site (for reference)                                                                   
                                                                                                  
  - Old repo: addyanddaddy/med-aside-v2                                                           
  - Old stack: Static HTML/CSS, no framework, no build process                                    
  - Old integrations: Web3Forms, Cloudinary (cloud: dmf1c5wvq), Tawk.to (widget:                  
  69aa5552ddd7fc1c34851406/1jj0lqiqk), GTM (GTM-K9XWG7GT)

  - Old branding: "MED ASIDE" (now "MED VEST")

  ---                                                                                             
  Design Direction: Warm & Human
                                                                                                  
  Color Palette                                                                    
                                                                                                  
  Background Primary:   #faf7f2 (warm cream/linen)                                                
  Background Secondary: #f5efe6 (light warm)
  Background Accent:    #f0ebe2 (warm highlight)                                                  
  Surface:              #ffffff (cards)                                            
  Text Primary:         #2c1810 (deep warm brown)                                                 
  Text Secondary:       #8b7355 (muted brown)                                      
  Text Tertiary:        #b3a18a (light brown)  
  Accent Primary:       #8b5e3c (warm brown)              
  Accent Secondary:     #b37d4e (copper/caramel)
  Accent Light:         #d4c5a9 (soft gold)               
  CTA/Dark:             #2c1810 (deep brown for buttons, dark sections)
  Success:              #2d6a4f (green for compliance badges)                                     
  Border:               #e8dfd3                                                                   
                                                                                                  
  Typography                                                                                      
                                                                                                  
  - Headlines: Playfair Display (serif) — warmth, trust, authority                 
  - Body: Inter (sans-serif) — clean, readable                                                    
  - Mobile-first sizing: H1 2rem→3.5rem, H2 1.5rem→2.5rem, H3 1.25rem→1.75rem                     
                                                                                                  
  Design Principles                                                                               
                                                                                                  
  - Soft rounded corners (12-16px cards, 24px buttons)                                            
  - Subtle shadows, no hard borders                                                               
  - Generous whitespace                                                                           
  - Warm, human photography                                                                       
  - Smooth scroll animations (fade-in, gentle lifts)                               
  - Mobile-first: 375px base, breakpoints at 640/768/1024/1280px
  - Bilingual: EN/ES with language toggle in nav                                                  
  - "Hablamos Español" prominent in CTAs

  - src/components/ui/Button.tsx — Polymorphic button (primary/secondary/outline/dark, 3 sizes,
  internal/external links)                                                                        
  - src/components/ui/SectionHeader.tsx — Reusable section header with label, title, accent,
  subtitle                                                                                        
  - src/components/ui/Card.tsx — Card with optional hover effect
  - src/components/ui/Accordion.tsx — Expandable FAQ accordion with animation                     
  - src/components/ui/AnimateIn.tsx — Framer Motion scroll-triggered animation wrapper
  (up/down/left/right)                                                                            
  - src/components/ui/StickyMobileCTA.tsx — Fixed bottom bar for mobile (Call + Get Started)      
                                                                                                  
  Homepage Sections ✅                                                                            
                                                          
  - src/components/sections/Hero.tsx — Animated hero with CTA buttons and phone number            
  - src/components/sections/StatsStrip.tsx — $500M+ / 5,000+ families / 100% compliance           
  - src/components/sections/HowItWorks.tsx — 4-step process grid with icons
  - src/components/sections/ServicesGrid.tsx — 5 service cards linking to individual pages        
  - src/components/sections/CaseResults.tsx — 6 case result cards with amounts and descriptions   
  - src/components/sections/Testimonials.tsx — Featured testimonial + 3-card grid with star       
  ratings                                                                                         
  - src/components/sections/FAQPreview.tsx — 4 FAQ accordion items + link to full FAQ page        
  - src/components/sections/CTABand.tsx — Dark CTA section with phone + schedule buttons +
  "Hablamos Español"                                                                              
                                                                                                  
  Homepage Page ✅                                        
                                                                                                  
  - src/app/[locale]/page.tsx — Full homepage assembling all 8 sections with 4 JSON-LD structured 
  data schemas:                                                                                   
    - Organization schema                                                                         
    - LocalBusiness schema                                                                        
    - FAQPage schema                                                                              
    - WebSite schema                                                                              
                                                                                                  
  SEO Infrastructure ✅                                                                           
                                                                                                  
  - src/components/seo/JsonLd.tsx — Reusable JSON-LD structured data component
  - src/app/sitemap.ts — Dynamic sitemap with 15 routes × 2 locales + hreflang alternates         
  - src/app/robots.ts — robots.txt with allow/disallow rules
                                                                                                  
  Data Files ✅                                           
                                    
  - src/lib/data.ts — Case results (6), testimonials (5 with EN/ES), home FAQ items (4 with EN/ES)
  - src/lib/content.ts — ALL page content for every page (About, Services ×5, How It Works,       
  Results, FAQ ×18, Legal, Contact, Portal) in EN/ES      
  - src/lib/blog-content.ts — 5 full blog articles (~500-800 words each) in EN/ES with slugs,     
  metadata, reading times                                                                         
                                               
  ---                                                                                             
  What Still Needs to Be Built           
                                                                                                  
  Remaining Pages (Priority Order)       
                                                                                                  
  1. Service pages (5) — Create src/app/[locale]/services/[slug]/page.tsx or individual pages. Use
   content from src/lib/content.ts → servicePages array. Each needs: hero, benefits, explanation, 
  process steps, FAQ with schema, CTA with GHL form.      
  2. About page — Create src/app/[locale]/about/page.tsx. Content in content.ts → aboutContent.   
  Sections: hero, story, mission/values, team, credentials, service area, CTA.
  3. How It Works page — Create src/app/[locale]/how-it-works/page.tsx. Content in content.ts →   
  howItWorksContent. Sections: hero, 4-step timeline, what to expect, portal preview, FAQ, CTA.
  4. Results page — Create src/app/[locale]/results/page.tsx. Content in content.ts →
  resultsContent. Aggregate stats, case studies grid with filter by service type.
  5. Testimonials page — Create src/app/[locale]/testimonials/page.tsx. Data in data.ts →         
  testimonials. Featured + grid, Review schema.                                                   
  6. FAQ page — Create src/app/[locale]/faq/page.tsx. Content in content.ts → faqContent. Grouped 
  accordion, full FAQ schema.                                                                     
  7. Contact page — Create src/app/[locale]/contact/page.tsx. Content in content.ts →
  contactContent. GHL form embed, booking calendar, business info, HIPAA notice.                  
  8. Portal page — Create src/app/[locale]/portal/page.tsx. Content in content.ts → portalContent.
   GHL client portal embed/redirect, features overview.                                           
  9. Legal page — Create src/app/[locale]/legal/page.tsx. Content in content.ts → legalContent.
  Privacy, Terms, HIPAA, Accessibility sections.                                                  
  10. Blog/Resources — Create src/app/[locale]/resources/page.tsx and
  src/app/[locale]/resources/[slug]/page.tsx. Content in blog-content.ts. Article listing,        
  individual article pages with Article schema.                   
                                                                                                  
  GHL Integration                                                 
                                                                                                  
  1. API Routes — Create src/app/api/ghl/contact/route.ts and src/app/api/ghl/referral/route.ts.
  These receive form submissions from the frontend and forward to GHL API to create contacts +    
  opportunities. Key pattern:                                     
  POST /api/ghl/contact → GHL Create Contact + Create Opportunity                                 
  2. GHL Client Library — Create src/lib/ghl.ts with functions: createContact(),
  createOpportunity(), uploadDocument(). Uses GHL_API_KEY env var.                                
  3. Contact Form Component — Create src/components/forms/ContactForm.tsx. Client component with
  validation, submits to /api/ghl/contact.                                                        
  4. Case Referral Form — Create src/components/forms/CaseReferralForm.tsx. Multi-field form with 
  file upload, submits to /api/ghl/referral.                      
  5. Chat Widget — Add GHL chat widget embed script to locale layout (replaces Tawk.to). Get embed
   code from GHL sub-account → Sites → Chat Widget.               
  6. Booking Calendar — Embed GHL calendar iframe on contact page. Set up calendar in GHL         
  sub-account first.                                      
  7. Client Portal — Embed or redirect to GHL client portal on portal page.                       
                                                                                                  
  SEO Finalization                                                                                
                                                                                                  
  1. Structured data on all pages — Add Service schema to service pages, HowTo schema to How It
  Works, Article schema to blog posts, Review/AggregateRating to testimonials.                    
  2. Meta tags audit — Ensure every page has unique title (under 60 chars), description (under 160
   chars), OG tags, Twitter Card tags.                                                            
  3. 301 redirects — In next.config.mjs, add redirects from old URL patterns (if old site had
  indexed pages).                                                                                 
  4. OG images — Create or migrate Open Graph images for social sharing.
  5. Performance optimization — Run Lighthouse, optimize images, ensure Core Web Vitals targets   
  (LCP < 2.5s, FID < 100ms, CLS < 0.1).                           
                                                                                                  
  Polish & Animations                                                                             
                                                                  
  1. Page transitions — Framer Motion AnimatePresence for route transitions.                      
  2. Scroll-triggered animations — Already have AnimateIn component, apply to all page sections.  
  3. Testimonial carousel — Add swipe support for mobile.         
  4. Number counter animation — Animate stat numbers counting up on scroll.                       
  5. Image placeholders — Add blur placeholder images for next/image.

  ---                                                                                             
  How to Continue Building                                        
                                                                                                  
  Local Development                                                                               
                                                                                                  
  npm install                                                                                     
  npm run dev                                                     
  # Visit http://localhost:3000/en (English)                                                      
  # Visit http://localhost:3000/es (Spanish)                                                      
                                                                  
  Deployment                                                                                      
                                         
  1. Connect this repo to Vercel                                                                  
  2. Set environment variables in Vercel project settings (see above)
  3. Add custom domain: medvst.com                                                                
  4. Every push to main auto-deploys     
                                               
  Building Remaining Pages                                
                                                                                                  
  All content is already written in src/lib/content.ts and src/lib/blog-content.ts. The page
  components just need to be created to consume this data. The homepage                           
  (src/app/[locale]/page.tsx) is the template — follow the same pattern for all other pages.
                                                                                                  
  GHL Integration                                                 
                                                                                                  
  The GHL sub-account is set up and the API key works. The API routes need to be created to proxy 
  form submissions to GHL. The chat widget embed code needs to be obtained from the GHL dashboard
  (Sites → Chat Widget) and added to the locale layout.                                           
                                                                  
  ---                                                                                             
  Important Notes                                                 
                                                                                                  
  1. NEVER commit .env.local — it contains the GHL API key
  2. All "MED ASIDE" references are WRONG — the brand is "MED VEST"
  3. All "medaside.com" references are WRONG — the domain is "medvst.com"
  4. Target audience is regular people, NOT lawyers — tone should be warm, reassuring, plain      
  language                                                        
  5. Mobile-first always — design for 375px first, scale up                                       
  6. Spanish is a first-class citizen — not an afterthought, full parity with English
  7. The old site repo (addyanddaddy/med-aside-v2) is for reference only — do not build on it
  8. Build was not verified locally — disk space ran out on the dev environment. First build will
  happen on Vercel or a machine with more disk space. Expect TypeScript errors that need fixing on
   first build.
